▲Dentsu, Berlin, 9th - Movie star Charlie Chaplin arrived in Berlin on the 9th and received a warm welcome from the public. Chaplin told a Domei News Agency reporter that he plans to go to Moscow from Berlin, then to Tokyo via Siberia. He will probably arrive in Tokyo before April, and after staying in Japan and touring various places, he will visit Shanghai and two or three other cities in China.

Important News

First Day of Commemoration for Martyred Soldiers in the Capital

(1) Venue Arrangement

(2) Ceremony Protocol

(3) Order of Public Memorial Service

(4) Key Attendees

(5) Tribute Offerings

(6) Central Party Headquarters Memorial Oration

(7) National Government Memorial Oration

(8) General Commander Chiang’s Memorial Oration

(9) Deputy Commander Zhang’s Memorial Oration

Today (the 10th), at 8:00 AM, in the Banbian Street Public Sports Ground in the capital, a grand memorial service was held for the soldiers who died in battle against the rebellion in the Army, Navy, and Air Force. The preparation was initiated by the Commander-in-Chief, and the ceremony was extremely solemn. The atmosphere throughout the venue was somber and dignified, evoking reverence. A detailed account of the various aspects is provided below:

▲ Venue Arrangement: At the main entrance and side entrances of the venue, plain cloth arches were erected, adorned with plain-colored paper floral decorations, bearing inscriptions such as "Memorial Service." A few steps from the main entrance, a tent was constructed using green and white cloth, housing registration desks for Central Committee members and officials from various levels of party headquarters, registration desks for senior officials of the National Government and various Yuan and ministries, registration desks for military representatives and foreign guests, and a speech platform for Chairman Chiang.

Registration desks for representatives of civilian organizations, educational institutions, and the press were set up separately on the left side of the entrance. The perimeter of the venue was enclosed with lengths of green and white cloth on the existing wooden railings, forming a circular shape. In the center of the venue, a martyrs' memorial pavilion was constructed of varnished white wood, with the words "Sacrificed for the Country" inscribed in black ink on all four sides. Opposite the pavilion was a sacrificial altar, with a horizontal banner presented by the Central Political Conference bearing the inscription "Mourning This National Tragedy." On the left and right walls in front of the altar, the four large characters "Eternal Righteousness" were inscribed. Inside the pavilion hung a portrait of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen and the flags of the Party and the Nation. On the left and right were arranged portraits of senior officers who died in the suppression of the rebellion. In the center of the hall was placed the memorial tablet for the soldiers of the Army, Navy, and Air Force who died in the suppression of the rebellion. On either side of the sacrificial table were floral wreaths presented by the Central Executive Committee and the Central Supervisory Committee. Lists of the names of officers and soldiers from various armies and divisions who died in the suppression of the rebellion were hung on the front wall of the memorial hall, attached to extremely long white cloths, written in regular script with black ink. High on both sides hung numerous eulogies from central government and national government agencies, as well as party headquarters and governments of various provinces and cities, with eloquent wording. It is estimated that the total number of eulogistic couplets throughout the venue was no less than ten thousand. The number of floral wreaths and other offerings was also substantial. Behind the altar were separate areas for the military band to rest, a broadcasting station, a tea area, and first-aid facilities.

▲ Ceremony Protocol: (A) Opening Ceremony: (1) Central Committee members, the Chairman and members of the National Government, the heads of various Yuan, the heads of various ministries, members of party headquarters at all levels, and representatives of various civilian organizations paid respects before the tablets of the fallen soldiers. (2) A gun salute was fired (the Army and Navy fired a 33-gun memorial salute). (3) Attendees took their positions. (4) Mournful music was played. (5) Three bows were made to the national flag, the party flag, the portrait of the late Premier, and the fallen soldiers. (6) The late Premier's will was read aloud. (7) Three minutes of silence were observed. (8) Flowers were offered. (9) A memorial oration was read. (10) A Central Committee member delivered a speech. (11) A National Government member delivered a speech. (12) The Commander-in-Chief delivered a speech. (13) Representatives from various military and political agencies delivered speeches. (14) Representatives from party headquarters at all levels delivered speeches. (15) Representatives from various civilian organizations delivered speeches. (16) Representatives from various armies and divisions delivered speeches. (17) The entire assembly shouted slogans. (18) Mournful music was played. (19) The ceremony concluded. (B) Public Memorial Service: (1) Attendees took their positions. (2) Mournful music was played. (3) Flowers were offered. (4) A memorial oration was read. (5) A moment of silence was observed. (6) Three bows were made. (7) Mournful music was played. (8) The ceremony concluded.

▲ Order of Public Memorial Service: Today was the first day of the public memorial service for various government agencies. The order of participation was as follows: (1) Central Committee members and all staff of the Central Party Headquarters (10:00 AM); (2) National Government members and all staff (10:20 AM); (3) Executive Yuan (10:40 AM); (4) Legislative Yuan (11:00 AM); (5) Judicial Yuan (11:20 AM); (6) Examination Yuan (11:40 AM); (7) Control Yuan (12:00 PM); (8) General Headquarters and its subordinate agencies (12:20 PM); (9) Ministry of Military Affairs and its subordinate agencies (12:40 PM); (10) Ministry of the Navy and its subordinate agencies (1:00 PM); (11) General Staff Headquarters and its subordinate agencies (2:20 PM); (12) Directorate General of Military Training and its subordinate agencies (2:40 PM); (13) Central Military Academy (3:00 PM); (14) Garrison Headquarters (3:20 PM); (15) Capital Police Department (3:40 PM); (16) Fortress Headquarters (4:00 PM); (17) National Government Guard Division (4:20 PM); (18) Representatives from other military and political agencies and various armies and divisions (4:40 PM).

▲ Key Attendees: This morning, key figures from the Central Government, the National Government, and various agencies attended, including Chiang Kai-shek, Yu Youren, Wu Jingheng, Wang Chonghui, Sun Ke, Shao YuanChong, Song Ziwen, Song Meiling, Liu Shangqing, Zhu Peide, Wang Boqun, Wang Zhengting, Kong Xiangxi, Chen Shaokuan, Chen Lifu, Liu Luyin, Zhu Jiahua, Ye Chucang, Ma Chaojun, Ru Yuli, Zhou Qigang, Shao Lizhi, Yu Jingtang, Gu Zhenglun, Wu Siyu, and others, as well as representatives from party headquarters at all levels and various civilian organizations, totaling approximately three thousand people.

▲ Tribute Offerings: The main officiant of the ceremony was Chiang Kai-shek, Chairman of the National Government and Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force. Yu Youren, Wang Chonghui, Sun Ke, and Shao YuanChong, members of the Central Committee and the National Government, assisted in the ceremony, which was conducted according to protocol. Chiang Kai-shek personally presented a floral wreath and read the memorial oration. Following that, Yu Youren, a member of the Central Committee, delivered a speech, stating that since the National Revolutionary Army set out from Guangdong, it had fought hundreds of battles, large and small. Many revolutionary comrades had sacrificed themselves for the Party and the Nation. In particular, during the recent rebellion of Yan and Feng, the Central Government launched a punitive expedition that lasted for several months, representing an unprecedentedly large-scale war. Numerous armed comrades sacrificed themselves for the Party, the Nation, and the Three Principles of the People. As the saying goes, "A man of firm resolve and benevolence will not seek life at the expense of benevolence, but will sacrifice his life to achieve it." General Commander Chiang endured hardship and difficulty, and amidst danger and turmoil, he led his comrades in diligent struggle to create a second China. This is a war history of the greatest commemorative value. Now that the major culprits have been eliminated, we must, after the pain subsides, reflect on the heroic deeds of the fallen generals and soldiers, continue the legacy of the martyrs, and realize the Three Principles of the People with a consistent spirit, fulfilling the purpose of peaceful unification. In this way, we can fulfill the responsibilities of those who live on and console the spirits of the martyrs. Anyone who undermines the Three Principles of the People and peaceful unification will be eradicated with full force. Next, Wang Chonghui, a member of the National Government, delivered a speech, stating that today's memorial service is an event that is both deeply sorrowful and profoundly meaningful. What did the martyrs die for? They died for the Three Principles of the People, for saving the Chinese nation. Those who have died are gone, their bodies may have perished, but their spirit is forever irreplaceable. After leaving this gathering, we must constantly remember the pain of their sacrifice, never forget their spirit of struggle, and resolve together to continue our efforts to fulfill their unfulfilled aspirations and console their heroic souls. Next, General Commander Chiang Kai-shek delivered a speech, stating that it has been six years since the National Revolutionary Army began its expedition. The suffering endured by the martyrs who died and the generals and soldiers who participated in the battles during this period has been both great and immense. This kind of suffering cannot be fully understood by those who have not participated in the battles. In 1926, the Communists attempted to overthrow the Kuomintang in Guangdong. At that time, the arrogance of the Communists was not only capable of oppressing Guangdong but also of oppressing the entire China. At that time, the generals and soldiers in Guangdong tried their best to resist. During the crisis, I summoned Commander-in-Chief Liu Zhi for a talk, vowing to fight the Communists to the death, and even saying that we might never meet again. The sorrow at that time was unknown to outsiders. As for the Jinan Incident, the pain was even more indescribable. At that time, all the generals and soldiers in Jinan were willing to die in Jinan, confronting the Japanese imperialists. The tragic situation and the spirit of unwavering courage in the face of danger were most gratifying. It was through this kind of sincerity that the foundation left by the late Premier could be maintained, allowing us to continue to complete the revolutionary work. However, we should be aware that in the successive battles, the remains of the comrades who have died have not yet been buried, and the parents, wives, and orphaned children they left behind have not been fully cared for. Before Tang Shengzhi's rebellion, he visited the school for orphans and widows and said that he would never again engage in mutual slaughter. But how long did it take before Tang betrayed us again, causing countless more soldiers to sacrifice their lives? Today, as we commemorate the fallen soldiers, we firmly believe that it will bring comfort to the families of our deceased comrades, that we will regard the parents and children of our deceased comrades as our own parents and children, and that we will fully shoulder and continue to strive for the unfulfilled aspirations of our deceased comrades. Only in this way can we console the spirits of the martyrs. If anyone still harbors ideas of power and self-interest, they are not true revolutionary soldiers. As for the compensation for the deceased comrades, the care for their families, the burial of their remains, and the resettlement of the disabled, preparations have already been made. I am presenting a report today. Since the beginning of the Northern Expedition, over the past six years, more than 300,000 soldiers have died. Last year, during the rebellion of Yan and the suppression of the communist bandits, approximately 2,480 officers and 34,453 soldiers died, and over 70,000 were wounded. The First, Second, Sixth, Seventh, Eighth, Ninth, Eleventh, Seventeenth, and Eighteenth Divisions, as well as the First Training Division, suffered the greatest losses, with an average of over 2,000 deaths per division, not including the wounded. Regarding the issue of compensation, the Ministry of Military Affairs has telegraphed to various provinces, cities, and counties to ensure full disbursement, totaling over 20 million. In the future, after the communist bandits have been completely eradicated and financial unification has been achieved, alternative compensation measures will be sought. Furthermore, preparations are underway for a cemetery for the fallen soldiers, which has already begun construction at Linggu Temple. Regarding the resettlement of disabled soldiers, a new village has been organized, capable of accommodating 5,000 to 10,000 people, so that the families of the disabled can also be accommodated. Plans are also being made to organize manufacturing facilities based on the degree of disability, so that they can have appropriate work. Regarding the resettlement of families of the deceased, a school for the families of the deceased has been established, currently divided into male and female schools, with over 500 students. The above is only a general report, and a detailed report will be issued in writing in the near future. Next, Wu Jingheng, a member of the Central Committee, and representatives from various military and political agencies, party headquarters at all levels, civilian organizations, and armies and divisions delivered speeches in succession. Then, under the leadership of General Commander Chiang, the entire assembly shouted slogans, and the ceremony was declared concluded.

▲ Central Party Headquarters Memorial Oration: On March 10, the twentieth year of the Republic of China, the entire members of the Central Executive Committee and the Central Supervisory Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang, along with party members, respectfully offer fresh flowers and pure libations to the spirits of the soldiers of the Army, Navy, and Air Force who died in the suppression of the rebellion. The oration reads: Illustrious soldiers, the heroes of our Party, who for the revolution of the people, pledged loyalty and sincerity, obeyed orders in Lingnan, and pacified the Central Plains. Having experienced hundreds of battles, they considered hardship insignificant, shed blood in the wilderness, and sacrificed themselves for the Party and the Nation. Driven by the principles, their armies were bound to conquer. Alas, soldiers, may your souls be aware that the suppression of the rebellion was a righteous campaign, and that righteousness makes the army strong, frightening the rebellious bandits into flight. Our soldiers fought fiercely on the battlefield, their精 [energy/essence] piercing the sun, their will as sharp as autumn frost. Demonstrating loyalty and sincerity, they attacked with vigor, never retreating despite setbacks, ultimately crushing the masses of enemies. Scaling city walls and breaching enemy lines, they split their brains and stained the earth with their livers, holding their spears to defend the country, not hesitating to sacrifice their bodies. The battle has just ended, the war chariot has temporarily ceased, but the brave soldiers have not returned, and our grief is boundless. Who will seek their armor? We establish a household waiting for their ennoblement, and recite an invocation to summon their souls in vain, with no way to stem our tears. Achieving benevolence by seeking it, we have heard the ancient maxim that though the body perishes, the name endures, so there is no resentment or anger. Fragrant offerings of orchids and gui are presented, and libations are poured. May the spirits accept them, and come to partake in their honor. Accept our offering.

▲ National Government Memorial Oration: On March 10, the twentieth year of the Republic of China, all the staff of the Civil Service Department, the Military Affairs Department, and the Accounting Department of the National Government respectfully offer fragrant incense to the spirits of the soldiers of the Army, Navy, and Air Force who died in the suppression of the rebellion. The oration reads: Alas, amidst the trials and tribulations of thunder and rain, and the dimness of heaven and earth, if there were not a multitude of talents, who could quell the great disaster? The noble soldiers are loyal and brave without equal, sacrificing themselves in an instant for a righteousness that will last a thousand autumns. The Northern Expedition was successful, and the foundations of the nation were newly laid, but the remnants of evil spread rampantly, relying on arms to incite chaos. Our comrades, with one heart and ten thousand minds, held a sincerity that pierced gold and stone, and a spirit that rose through the wind and clouds. Pacifying Guangdong and Hunan in the south, and leveling Henan and Hebei in the north, with fierce and swift advances, they competed to engage in hand-to-hand combat. Wading through floodwaters that reached their ankles, scorched by the sun, suffering wounds and exposing blood, they regarded death as returning home, fighting to the death together. Amidst a hail of bullets and a forest of guns, they pressed on relentlessly, falling one after another but never ceasing, their spirit reaching a point of invincibility. Their blood stained the wild grass, their bones lay exposed in the Central Plains. Their heroic spirit rode the clouds, their loyal souls transformed into cranes, their blue blood and green phosphorus filling the desolate landscape. Not boasting of courage and strength, they revered the principles, living as patriots and dying as heroic spirits. Military prowess was displayed and cruel tyranny was finally vanquished, the sun shines again and the rivers and mountains are once again settled. As for the brave warriors, following the storms, following the mountains. Recalling their heroic deeds, our hearts are filled with boundless sorrow. Sad music echoes, fragrant flowers glow brilliantly. Return, O spirits, and grant us your blessings. Accept our offering.

▲ General Commander Chiang’s Memorial Oration: On this, the tenth day of March in the twentieth year of the Republic of China, Chiang Chung-cheng, Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, leading all military officers, reverently offers incense, flowers, and pure libations to the spirits of the fallen soldiers, saying: Alas, since the rise of our National Revolutionary Army to this day, it has been six years. Those who came before us include the late Premier and the late Party Representative Liao Zhongkai, and those who came after us include Cai Guangju, Liu Yaochen, and the more than 300,000 martyrs of officers, soldiers, and students, all of whom died before us. Though their deaths differed, they all died for the battles of our army and the principles of our party. Moreover, the tragedy and heroism of their deaths are sorrowful and painful. Though months or even years have passed, their spirits still seem to linger around us in our dreams, and we cannot forget them. Especially on moonlit nights when marching across the battlefield, we still feel a sense of kinship and love, as if they were members of our family, fathers and sons, constantly by our side. We are not even aware of why this is so. Alas, what in the world is more unbearable and intolerable than this? The rise of our army began with the Eastern Expedition against the rebellious Chen Jiongming and ended with the Northern Expedition against the traitor Yan Xishan. The battles fought in between, though only covering six years, extended across a vast territory, from east to west, from south to north, going back and forth, totaling over 20,000 li. In the spring of 1925, there were the battles of Danshui, Huizhou, Mianhu, Hepo, and Xingning. In the autumn of the same year, we returned to Guangzhou to suppress Yang Ximin and Liu Zhenhuan and to eliminate the remnants of Chen Jiongming's forces in the south. In the summer of 1926, we launched the Northern Expedition, including the battles of Tingsi Bridge on the Xiang-E Road, Mahui Ridge and Tujiapu on the Nanxun Road, as well as the siege of Nanchang and the siege of Wuchang, and the battles of Zhejiang and Anhui in the south. In the spring of 1927, there were the battles on the Jinpu and Pinghan lines. In the summer, there were the battles of Xuzhou and Longtan. In the spring of 1928, there were the battles of Jinan and Lincheng. In the spring of 1929, there was the battle of Wuhan. In mid-autumn, there were the battles of Dengfeng and Linru. In late autumn, there were the battles of Huaxian and Liangguang. In the winter, there was the expedition against Tang Shengzhi in Zhumadian. And then, in 1930, Yan Xishan rebelled and conspired, leading to the great battles on the Longhai, Pinghan, Jinpu, and Xiang-E four lines, as well as the armies dispatched to suppress the rebellion in Yunnan and Guangdong. The scale and intensity of these battles, in which I personally led the troops on the front lines, shared the hardships and dangers with our martyrs, and fought to the death together, numbered over a hundred. Alas, the poisonous flames reached the sky, causing rashes and diseases. In the barren land, the wind was sorrowful and the sun was dim. Whenever I read Li Hua's lines about snow covering the ankles, frost on the beard, inadequate warmth from cotton clothing, and fingers splitting from the cold, I cannot help but feel the grief that has been shared throughout history. In my youth, I often recited the words, "The soul is bound, the sky is dark and gloomy; ghosts and spirits gather, the clouds are thick and dense." I always felt an overwhelming sense of sorrow and grief. Who would have known that I would actually experience this myself, as I do today? The heartbreak and anguish are as if my flesh were being cut and pierced. However, the tragedy of the martyrs' deaths, the loyalty of their service, the courage of their self-sacrifice, and the unity of their lives and deaths are not only mourned by the people of the world and revered by the Party and the Nation, but are also seen, heard, and respected by countries in the East and West. However, the most tragic and sorrowful thing is that there are things that cannot be seen or heard by others, known only between the dead and the living, and yet cannot be spoken of or tolerated by the living. The grief and sorrow of this cannot be described by words or ink. What is the reason for this? It is the sincere spirit that even ghosts and gods weep for. As for the Shaji Incident on June 23, the anti-communist incident on March 20, and the Jinan Incident on May 3, the officers and soldiers who participated in those events either died or were wounded. Those who did not die, such as Commander-in-Chief Liu Zhi, who received orders in Dongshan to eliminate the communists, and Brigade Commander Li Yannian, who resolutely defended Jinan, recall the situation at that time of entrusting life in danger, of unwavering courage in the face of difficulty, and of the lingering sorrow of a farewell to the dead. The feelings were especially beyond the comprehension of outsiders and the endurance of ordinary people. Alas, the loyal hearts and the sincerity moved ghosts and gods and shook heaven and earth. This is truly the most tragic and sorrowful history of our Party and our army. It is through the accumulation of hundreds of thousands of heroes and martyrs that we have achieved the unified situation of today. Who knows that it was formed by the unwavering sincerity of the soldiers in a way that is unseen, unheard, unknown, and unnoticed? However, even this most tragic and sorrowful thing can still be described by us, the survivors, in a small way, to leave behind the admiration of later generations and the families of the deceased. As for enduring insults and tolerating shame to attract unexpected slander and lifelong grievances, not only can people not hear, see, or know, but even those involved could not have imagined it in their dreams. How much greater is the grief and sorrow of this? Alas, I have experienced a history of pain that has never been seen before and encountered a tragic situation that has never been seen in the world, and all of this has converged on me alone. How much greater is the hidden pain and suffering in my heart? Sadly, the heat and cold, freezing and scorching, hunger, thirst, and exhaustion are all hardships that ordinary people cannot endure, but our soldiers have endured them all. The horrors of cutting open abdomens and gouging out eyes, cutting off arms and amputating legs, unheard of in the world, have all been suffered by our soldiers. They regard the suffering of the Premier as their own family suffering, and the public grievances of the Party and the Nation as their personal grievances. They endure national humiliation that others cannot endure, and suffer party shame that others cannot accept. They leave their parents, bid farewell to their wives, fall one after another, regard death as returning home, and have no regrets. Why is this? It is because the late Premier's teachings on loving each other with sincerity are accumulated in their hearts and manifested in their actions. Alas, the dead are gone, but how can the living bear it? Who does not have parents, with white hair in the hall, waiting to be cared for? Who does not have a wife, a widow in the room, who still needs to be raised? Whenever I think of the parents of the soldiers, they are my own parents. The families of the martyrs are the families of the Premier. The reason why we, the survivors, endure shame without regret and tolerate death for a moment is only because the remains have not yet been buried and the families have not been cared for. It is not just because the revolution has not been completed and the principles have not been realized. As the ancients said, "While there is still breath, this aspiration will not cease." I will only exhaust the unfulfilled responsibilities of the deceased and strive to complete the unfulfilled aspirations of the martyrs. Alas, death can be heavier than Mount Tai or lighter than a feather. As the ancients said, "Sacrificing oneself to achieve benevolence" and "Though dead, still alive," the martyrs died to fight for the survival of the Party and the Nation, to fight for the independence of the nation, to die for the revolution, to die for the principles, to die for unification. What is there to regret in death? In the world, no one can escape death, only in dying in the right place. Death is as good as dying with righteous people, and death is to be included in the ranks of righteousness, so one does not lose one's righteous destiny. The deaths of the martyrs were all in the ranks of revolutionary soldiers and in the midst of the Premier's principles. The glory of their death is enough to illuminate China and foreign countries and to be passed down through the ages. Why should I be sad? Why should I be sorrowful? I am only ashamed that we, the survivors, have not fulfilled our responsibilities as survivors, have not fulfilled the aspirations of the martyrs, report our face to the world, and feel guilty before the gods. We grieve for those who survive and are saddened by those who have not died, and we cannot help but offer sacrifices to the martyrs in order to sacrifice ourselves, those who survive. This is why we are sad and grieved, to mourn the tragedy of the deaths of our soldiers, and cannot restrain ourselves. Alas, with the spirits of the martyrs as witnesses, may this sincerity come and receive our offerings. Accept our offering.

▲ Deputy Commander Zhang’s Memorial Oration: On the tenth day of March in the twentieth year of the Republic of China, Zhang Xueliang, Deputy Commander of the Army, Navy, and Air Force, dispatched his representative, Yang Huancai, to respectfully offer fragrant wine and various sacrifices to the spirits of the soldiers who died in the suppression of the rebellion, saying: Alas, the country is in danger, and chaos flows rampant. Great vermin run amok, inciting the communist party, shaking the foundation of the nation, and endangering the laws of heaven. Rampaging through Shandong and Henan, poisoning Hubei and Hunan, the Chinese people were oppressed. Our army advanced to suppress them, vowing to sweep away the demonic forces and uphold the righteous path. Noble and courageous troops fight bravely, rushing to various provinces, battling for years. The army is sharp and unwavering, determined to knock down those aiming high, and to let eternal glory shine. We respectfully offer fresh flowers, and we use our sincerity to remember their fragrance. Alas, accept our offering.

Yu Youren's Report on the National Assembly and Provisional Constitution at the Memorial Week

Explaining the Necessity of Reform Today

At the Central Party Headquarters' memorial week on the 9th, Yu Youren reported on the "National Assembly and Provisional Constitution," with the following remarks: The convocation of the National Assembly is in accordance with the late Premier's will. As the opening date approaches, our party comrades should make every effort to ensure its success. Recalling the difficult and arduous circumstances when the Premier went north from Guangzhou and passed away in Beijing, and his ardent hope for the convocation of the National Assembly, it remains vivid in my mind. When the Premier went north, he issued a Northern Expedition Declaration, which outlined two objectives for convening the National Assembly: (1) to seek peace and unification within the country to resolve the people's livelihood issues, and (2) to abolish unequal treaties externally to enhance our international standing. It also explained the significance of convening the National Assembly as a combination of revolutionary military force and the people. The so-called revolutionary military force in the past referred to the failure of the revolutionary military to unify the country at that time. From the current perspective, it is to seek a combination of the government and the people. The function of this combination is: 1. From the perspective of the government itself, to seek the development of all work to meet the needs of the people. Only in this way can the benefits of work development accrue to the people. 2. From the perspective of the people, to enable the people to choose what they need. Only in this way can the needs of the people be fully expressed. The convocation of the National Assembly now is to realize this important meaning.

Last week, Committee Member Dai reported that "the tasks of the National Assembly are to make the Three Principles of the People clearly accepted by the people of the whole country in law, and to make the people of the whole country clearly recognize in law that the establishment of the Republic of China should be based on the Outline of National Reconstruction," and declared that "there should be a covenant between the government and the people." Now that the whole country has been peacefully unified, and during the period of political tutelage, in order to communicate the will between the government and the people, and to convene the National Assembly, the legal provisions regarding the relationship between the government and the people are indeed the most important task of the Assembly. Last week, the Central Provisional Standing Committee passed the establishment of the Provisional Constitution Drafting Committee, which shows that the Central Government is determined to have a Provisional Constitution. The first Provisional Constitution Drafting Meeting will be held this afternoon. Because our party comrades may have unclear understandings, I will explain this issue in detail to everyone again.

From the history of our party, from the Revive China Society to the Tongmenghui, from the Tongmenghui to the Chinese Revolutionary Party, from the Chinese Revolutionary Party to the Kuomintang. The Revive China Society was the initial stage, the Tongmenghui and the Chinese Revolutionary Party were the founding stages, and the Kuomintang was the mature stage. In each stage, during the time of the Tongmenghui, the Premier had already established his great propositions, such as the Three Principles of the People, the Five-Power Constitution, and the Three Stages of National Reconstruction, all of which were clearly announced. At that time, imperialism was invading the East, and the Chinese people were in a state of dormancy. The Premier was able to observe the national conditions internally and assess the overall situation externally, and create the Three Principles of the People, the Five-Power Constitution, and the Three Stages of National Reconstruction. This is not only a major event in China, but also a significant event worthy of commemoration in the world. However, everyone knows that the Three Principles of the People and the Five-Power Constitution were created exclusively by the Premier, while the Three Stages of National Reconstruction are often overlooked, and considered a very ordinary matter. In fact, it is also very difficult to invent. In ancient China, there was a distinction between the ages of disorder, rising peace, and great peace, which is found in the Gongyang Commentary. Also, in the Book of Rites, there is a distinction between the ages of Great Unity and Lesser Tranquility. When we read these books, we often skimmed over them, neglecting the creative essence of the ancient sages. Many years ago, the Premier, in the preface to Liu Chengyu's "History of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom," also gave an explanation of the revolutionary process: "First, the military government period, where sovereignty lies with the military government, and an ordinance is issued to the people; second, the tutelage period, where sovereignty lies with the government, and a jointly agreed covenant is established with the people; third, the constitutional government period, where sovereignty lies with the people, and a fully constitutional state is organized." He also lamented the death of Hong Xiuquan, saying that he did not understand the meaning of military government and constitutional government, which led to Zeng Guofan's奏成(helped complete) the Restoration of the Qing Dynasty. The Russian Revolution had what was called the New Economic Policy period, and the Communists admired Lenin's keen eye. In fact, they did not know that it was influenced by the Four Principles of the Tongmenghui in China. It can be said that they accepted the strategies indicated by the Premier to our party comrades. I have repeatedly cited examples from ancient and modern times, both Chinese and foreign, to prove the importance of the Three Stages of National Reconstruction, in order to make our party comrades deeply understand the late Premier's will, which says, "I have devoted myself to the national revolution for forty years." In these forty years, the Premier's revolutionary spirit has been completely consistent, and his general propositions have never been changed in the slightest. Those who follow it will be governed, and those who oppose it will be chaotic, which is inevitable. Therefore, to go a step further, from the Tongmenghui to the present day, the Premier's propositions have a binding force in the revolutionary process.

Since the success of the Northern Expedition, the voices for the National Assembly and the Provisional Constitution have risen. The Central Government has also discussed it several times. After the Fifth Plenary Session of the Second National Congress, the voices subsided. After the great war last year, the voices for the National Assembly and the Provisional Constitution were raised again by the people and the Central Government. After the Fourth Plenary Session of the Third National Congress, the voices also subsided. The Premier's division of the Three Stages of National Reconstruction, in the Tongmenghui, was military government, provisional constitution, and constitutional government, and in the revolutionary strategy, it was military government, tutelage government, and constitutional government. Changing provisional constitution to tutelage government did not change the proposition of the provisional constitution, because the word "tutelage" has a broader scope and can include everything. Therefore, the Premier also stated, "During the period of tutelage government, the provisional constitution will be implemented," and the words "not the current one" are noted in parentheses. He also explained painfully and clearly, pointing out the mistake of not following his revolutionary program in the first year of the Republic. The serious mistake of the Provisional Constitution of the first year of the Republic was that the legislators did not necessarily fully understand revolutionary doctrines, so the Provisional Constitution they drafted was completely separate from revolutionary doctrines, and was too far from what our party and the people demanded, and even had nothing to do with the legislators themselves. This kind of Provisional Constitution, which was separated from revolution, separated from the people, and separated from itself, was either outdated or transcended the times, so it became a relic of the Republic of China. In the Declaration of the Outline of National Reconstruction formulated by the Premier in the thirteenth year of the Republic, it was argued that the Provisional Constitution of the first year of the Republic did not go through the two stages of military government and tutelage government, so it could not have practical effect. It did not fundamentally deny the proposition of the Provisional Constitution in the national reconstruction program. Its meaning is that without going through the military government period, the counter-revolutionary forces cannot be eliminated, which puts military personnel at risk of abusing the provisional constitution. Without going through the tutelage government period, the people will be suddenly liberated and will not be able to understand the true meaning of the relationship between the provisional constitution and themselves. It refers to the fact that the first year of the Republic had neither escaped the military period nor achieved tutelage government. Now that the military has been pacified and tutelage government has achieved considerable results, it is time for our party to support democracy, and the situation is no longer the same as before. There is no longer a danger of those who oppose the revolution taking advantage of it, nor is there a deeply ingrained habit of abandoning responsibility. It is the right time to draft a provisional constitution to seek cooperation between the people and the government. In the past two years, some scholars who did not understand revolutionary doctrines embraced the theory of human rights and talked extensively about the provisional constitution. They did not know that the civil rights in the provisional constitution that the Premier referred to are revolutionary civil rights, which are completely different from the civil rights theories of religious figures and past politicians that they picked up. Today, I am explaining this meaning in the hope that everyone will conduct in-depth research on the provisional constitution issue and contribute to the Central Government to consolidate the foundation of peaceful unification and achieve long-term peace and stability.

Commencement of Sino-Japanese Railway Negotiations

▲ Gao Jiyi and Kimura Discuss the Results

▲ Will Assign Commissioners to Discuss Concrete Details

Shenyang Correspondence: Regarding the issue of Sino-Japanese railway negotiations, Kimura, director of the South Manchuria Railway (SMR), and Gao Jiyi, chairman of the Northeast Communications Committee, held their first meeting at the office of the Beining Railway at 3 p.m. yesterday. Irie Shotaro, director of the Fengtian office of the SMR, and Kimura Tatsuo, interpreter of the SMR office, accompanied Director Kimura to the meeting. On the Chinese side, in addition to Gao Jiyi, there were also Guo Xurun, director of the Jichang and Jidun Railways, and Yin Shousong, chief of the general affairs section of the Jichang and Jidun Railways. There was a very long discussion regarding the formal commencement of railway negotiations. It was agreed that both sides would assign commissioners to conduct concrete discussions. As for the assignment procedures, Guo Xurun representing Gao Jiyi and Irie Shotaro representing Director Kimura will hold their second meeting in the next two or three days. (March 6)

Liu Zerong, Special Commissioner of the Sino-Soviet Conference, Requests Leave to Return Home

▲ Accompanied by Staff Members Xie Yixing and Others

▲ Mo Dehui Arrives in Harbin from Liaoning

Harbin Correspondence: Mo Dehui, plenipotentiary of the Sino-Soviet Conference, who went to Beijing to seek instructions, returned from the capital and passed through Shenyang, where he stayed for several days. He departed from Shenyang by train on the evening of the 4th of this month and arrived in Changchun early on the 5th. He then transferred to a train to Harbin. However, when the special train passed through Shuangchengbao, it stopped for half a day to visit relatives and friends and pay respects at the graves. It was scheduled to arrive at about 6 p.m. on the 5th, and the Dong Railway sent a car to meet him, arriving in Harbin at about 7 p.m. Although Mo's departure abroad was scheduled for March 15 in Beijing, it is heard that due to delays in various matters and the fact that the Dong Railway Council still needs to convene a meeting before departure to solve recent road matters, he will not leave until late March at the earliest. Mo has already telegraphed diplomatic messengers to prepare various food items to be transported by train when he goes to Russia. Before Mo goes to Russia, Liu Zerong, the special commissioner acting as plenipotentiary, along with delegation staff members Xie Yixing, secretaries Feng Jie, Wu Jialu, Tao Guilin, and diplomatic messenger Fu Zhanyuan, returned to Harbin from Russia on the evening of the 4th of this month. Liu and others departed from Russia on the 24th of last month. The train was delayed along the way. It should have arrived in Harbin at 8:35 a.m. on the 4th, but it was delayed until 9:50 p.m. Those who arrived at the station to welcome them that night included Jin Ronggui, advisor to the Dong Railway Superintendent's Office, Li Shaogeng, acting director, Guo F绵監事長Fu Mian, supervisor, and 40 or 50 section chiefs from various departments. After Liu and others got off the train, they returned to their residences separately. At about 10 p.m. on the evening of the 4th, the reporter visited Liu Zerong at his residence at 花園街 Garden Street, Qinjiagang. According to his conversation, he and several colleagues returned home this time because the delegation had no important business after Plenipotentiary Mo returned home to seek instructions. At the beginning of their trip abroad, they did not expect to stay in Russia for such a long time and missed their hometowns. Therefore, they took a few days of leave before the Plenipotentiary returned to Russia to take a look. It is expected that they will not stay in the country for many days. When Plenipotentiary Mo goes to Russia, they will still accompany him. After my return, the affairs of the delegation will be temporarily handled jointly by the three gentlemen, Special Commissioners Wang Zengwei Juwei Zeng and Secretary Cai Yunchun. Before returning home, I saw Karahan off and told him that Plenipotentiary Mo had a definite date to go to Russia, which he was very pleased to hear. At the beginning of their stay in Russia, many members of the delegation suffered from acclimatization problems. Later, as they stayed in Russia for a long time, they no longer had this phenomenon. The climate in Moscow is very good. Even in the past winter, I heard that the temperature here had reached minus 46 degrees, but the coldest temperature in the Russian capital was only over 20 degrees. As for the future of the conference, it is difficult to predict. Each side has its own propositions. Whether the propositions of the two sides will be consistent in the future remains to be determined by future negotiations. However, after the proposal to proceed with group discussions, the difference is that the Russian side wants to discuss the issue of restoring diplomatic relations first, while our side wants to discuss the Dong Railway first. Although there are differences in the middle, it will not hinder the progress of the conference. (March 5)

Guangdong Central Bank Resumes Redemption of 50-Yuan Notes

Guangzhou Correspondence: After the Guangdong Central Bank temporarily suspended redemption on September 30 of the 18th year of the Republic, after the situation stabilized, all 100-yuan, 1-yuan, 5-yuan, and 10-yuan notes have been redeemed in installments. Recently, in addition to issuing military treasury and financial notes, the fund of the Central Bank has become sufficient again. It is estimated that the Central Bank has no less than 20 million in cash, while issuing about 30 million in banknotes. The ratio of reserves to the amount of issuance is 3 to 2. On the 5th of this month, it was announced that the 50-yuan notes that had not been redeemed would also be redeemed. From the time the bank stopped redeeming banknotes two years ago until yesterday, it can be said that all banknotes have been redeemed. At the same time, all branches and sub-branches in various places have unrestricted redemption. In the future, all tax revenues will be received in cash. In order to facilitate the redemption of banknotes, the Central Bank had previously notified the citizens that redeemers in the city could go to the West Embankment office or the Yonghan branch office to redeem them in full at any time. Unexpectedly, before and after the start of redemption, the Central Bank was quite crowded. In order to cope with the large number of redemptions, the Central Bank had prepared a large amount of cash for redemption and dispatched staff to the South Embankment headquarters and branches to assist in redemption. The measures were fairly smooth. According to Fan Qiwu, director of the Department of Finance, the Central Bank has issued about 20 to 30 million banknotes, and the Central Bank's fund is about 20 million yuan. In addition to more than 2 million being used for external loans, there are still 17 million yuan in the bank. With such sufficient cash in recent days, there is great confidence after the announcement of unrestricted redemption. Also, the reason for the rise in foreign currency yesterday was that the Guangdong Customs had collected too much foreign currency in taxes five days ago, resulting in an oversupply of foreign currency on the market, which caused the skyrocketing of foreign currency. In order to regulate finance, the authorities have not only continued to resume redemption in recent days, but also ordered the Guangdong Customs to receive Central Bank banknotes for all tax revenues from the 5th onwards, in order to facilitate circulation. In this situation, it is expected that the price of banknotes on the market will be restored in a few days. (March 6)

Rampancy of the Red Spear Society in Yicheng, Shanxi

▲ The Number of Bandits Reaches More Than 4,000

▲ Reported to Have Been Dispersed by Garrison Troops

Taiyuan Correspondence: Yicheng County in southern Shanxi has been invaded by Red Spear Society bandits from Henan Province. Because the county is a thoroughfare between Henan and Shanxi, many people from Henan reside there. The residents of Yicheng have the custom of practicing boxing due to the relationship of contamination, but they did not expect that practicing boxing would cause harm to the local area. This incident initially involved only 30 or 40 people, who started in mountain villages in the east of the city. Within a few days, the number grew from dozens to hundreds to more than 4,000. The speed of its spread and the magnitude of its momentum were even greater than the Boxer Rebellion of the Gengzi year. According to those who came from the county, when they left the county, the number of bandits had gathered to more than 4,000, occupying 70 or 80 villages. They ordered the residents of each village to supply rice, flour, red cloth, yellow tables, incense, cigarettes, wooden poles, spears, etc. They wore black clothes, wrapped red cloth around their heads, and carried spears. Some also carried firearms. They claimed to be blessed by a heavenly master, immune to guns and knives, and immune to gunpowder. They used the slogans of resisting taxes and eliminating harm for the people. There were both male and female bandits, both from Henan and Shanxi. When it first happened, the county police and militia immediately surrounded and suppressed them. Both sides engaged in battle and suffered deaths. Later, because the bandit forces were too large and the police force was no match, the county magistrate requested the local garrison troops of Zhang Renjie to assist in the suppression. Yang Chengyuan, who was stationed in Linfen, also sent a battalion of troops to assist in the suppression after receiving the report. However, the county has reported to the provincial government that the bandits have been wiped out by the garrison troops and county police. The people suffered great losses from this disaster. A certain gentleman Wang has been sent to the province to pay respects to the authorities and ask for instructions on how to deal with the aftermath. The county is about 700 miles away from the province. The provincial government has not received detailed information about the bandit situation in the county in recent days. We will investigate and report further. (March 6)

Henan Bandits Invade the Border of Woyang and Suxian

Bengbu Correspondence: Woyang and Suxian in northern Anhui have been plagued by bandits for years, which has become commonplace. Yang Xieyue, a major bandit in eastern Henan, recently colluded with local bandits in Woyang and Suxian and led more than 2,000 men into Anhui Province last month. They dispersed into small groups and harassed the border areas of Woyang and Suxian. The bandits have cannons, mortars, and machine guns, and their power is very rampant. Moreover, more than half of the group are defeated soldiers, so their actions are not comparable to ordinary local bandits. They first occupied the area around Genghuang Temple in Woyang. After the 270th Regiment of the 45th Division, led by Liu Zixin, launched a suppression campaign, Liu's regiment suffered minor losses due to the large number of bandits. Wei Lihuang then added the 1st Regiment of the Independent Brigade, led by Mei E, to intercept them from Bengbu. The Zhang Baoguo group of more than 1,000 bandits then directly invaded Suxian at the beginning of the month, while the rest still occupied the northeast area of Woyang. It is heard that Zhang Baoguo, nicknamed Zhang Dashen, is extremely fierce. When he arrived in Suxian, he was attacked by the 3rd District Defense Corps of the county at the Dawangmiao Bridge. After three hours of contact, dozens of bandits were killed and two hostages were rescued. The bandits fled north and burned down Hanzhai, Jiangyan, and Zhuzhuang before leaving. Later, they detoured through Miaohua area of Yongcheng County and transferred to Xudaowa and Kongzhuang, 20 miles west of Suixi in Suxian, and committed looting and kidnapping. At the same time, the Zhang Chuanwen gang of bandits in the county also disturbed Tangjiazhai, 35 miles northwest of Linhuan, and echoed Zhang Nian from afar, and contained the people's regiment from blocking and suppressing. Wang Xinlan, the county magistrate of Suxian, repeatedly reported the situation. He has now dispatched the county garrison team to suppress them at full speed and requested the 7th Division to draw a part to assist in the attack to prevent the bandits from fleeing east again. (March 8)

▲ The former Ganzhou bandits fled into Anhui, and the Anhui authorities sent troops to defend against them at Yinjiahui. Tunxi is extremely tense. The Huizhou Guild Hall in Wuhu convened an emergency meeting to request the authorities to send troops to block and suppress the bandits. ▲ Although the central government has repeatedly ordered the abolition of the rice inspection donation and salt levy surcharge established by the Anhui Provincial Government, the province still collects them as usual because it relies on them to subsidize military and political expenses. Because of too much accumulated rice, the rice merchants in Wuhu had to pay donations to export it. Recently, the Executive Yuan issued a strict order to abolish the Anhui Province rice and salt inspection fees on the same day, and the rice industry associations implemented strikes and stopped transportation the day before yesterday due to repeated telegrams of opposition from the Guangzhou Rice Industry Association. All transactions were stopped upstream and downstream of the river, and the situation suddenly became serious. The chief inspector of the round transport rice inspection immediately telegraphed the province to ask for instructions on how to deal with the situation. Zhao Jingshi, director of the Wuhu Public Security Bureau, Yu Yuying, the county magistrate, and leaders from all walks of life believed that the overall strike of the rice industry was related to the lives of thousands of workers and was extremely important to the security of the city. They also tried their best to mediate, and the situation was finally resolved last night. Work resumed today, and the condition was that rice and grain exports would not be subject to current donations for the time being and would be registered first pending a final resolution.

A Village Woman Dies in a Suzhou-Bound Train with Her Grandson: A resident of Daoshiguanbang, Qianzhou Town, 71st Tu, 15th District of the county, a Mrs. Tang Haofu, about fifty years old, took her three-year-old grandson to Suzhou to visit her three sons the day before yesterday. When the train arrived at Wangting Station, she suddenly fell ill and died. The station staff took the body and the three-year-old boy to the station and found a Shiqiao Wan train ticket on her. The railway police inquired at Shiqiao Wan without success and then went to Qianzhou to find relatives. Haofu learned of the incident, went to the scene, took his grandson back, and hired a boat to Wangting to have the body coffined and transported back for burial.

Commemorating the Martyrs Who Died in the Anti-Rebellion Campaign: Yesterday was the day to commemorate the martyrs of the army, navy, and air force who died in the anti-rebellion campaign. At 8:00 AM, over a thousand people from all walks of life gathered at the Wuxi Grand Theater for the memorial service. Zhang Hentian presided over the ceremony, which was conducted according to protocol.

Lawsuit Filed Regarding the Nantang Capsizing: Regarding the case of the Taichang Company's Hengyi steamboat sinking in Nantang, resulting in the drowning deaths of ten male and female passengers, the County Court Prosecutor's Office summoned the plaintiffs, Mrs. Mi Zhu, and the defendants in custody, Yang Xiangzhao, Lu Xingsheng, and Xiang Sanbao, for a court hearing the day before yesterday. Prosecutor Zhu Zonghai reviewed all the details and determined that while the sinking was caused by passengers rushing to disembark, causing the boat to tilt, and the driver's poor skills, the main cause was the boat being overloaded, exceeding the regulations. The defendants Yang Xiang, Lu Xingsheng, and Xiang Sanbao, through negligence in their duties, caused the steamboat to sink, drowning ten people. They should each be charged under Article 47 and Article 74, committing the crime in Article 291, Paragraph 2 of the same law. Yesterday, according to the Code of Criminal Procedure, a public prosecution was filed with the Criminal Division of the same court.

Restaurants Ordered to Collect Feast Tax: The restaurant industry in the city complained that the feast tax was affecting their business, and separately requested the Finance Bureau and the County Chamber of Commerce to stop collecting the tax on their behalf starting this month. Xu Shifa, the director of the feast tax collection, also applied to resign, and his guarantor, 丅 Xijun, also requested to withdraw the guarantee. Yesterday, the county government raised the matter at a county administrative meeting, which resolved: (1) Xu Shifa's resignation would be retained, but if he insisted, the Finance Bureau would appoint another person to handle it. (2) The arrears for January and February would be the responsibility of Xu Shifa and the original guarantor to clear in full by a deadline. (3) If the restaurant industry stopped collecting the tax without the approval of the competent authorities, the Finance Bureau would send personnel to audit the accounts and order the restaurants to compensate for all uncollected taxes. (4) The county government would issue a notice that the restaurant industry would continue to collect the education surtax on feasts according to regulations.

Zhenjiang

Preparing to Establish a Meteorological Testing Bureau: The Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau is actively proceeding with preparations for a meteorological testing project. The content of the main meteorological station is based on the regulations of the second-class meteorological station stipulated by the Central Meteorological Research Institute, with slight expansions. The testing items are divided into weather, air pressure, maximum and minimum temperature, humidity, rainfall, evaporation, wind direction, wind speed, cloud cover, cloud types, solar power, sunshine hours, grass temperature, and ground temperature. Meteorological sub-stations will be attached to the construction bureaus of each county to facilitate comparative research.

After investigation by the provincial government and transfer to the court, the investigation has concluded. Yesterday was the date of the second trial. Witnesses Qiao Yaotang and others were summoned and questioned for a long time. Cui's testimony was evasive, but he denied any fraudulent activities. Regarding the forgery of provincial orders, there are announcements to prove it. The trial lasted for three hours before adjourning. Cui Xinshan remains in custody pending the final verdict.

Changshu

The Case of the Seizure of Opium at Dayi Bridge Has Been Solved: On the evening of the 2nd of this month, two boats carrying a large quantity of opium passed through the city river of Dayi Bridge Town, Jiuzhe District, this county. Local hooligans learned of this and gathered many people to follow the boats to the edge of the market, where they drew pistols and carried out a robbery. As a result, the two boats' worth of opium was seized. It was not until the afternoon of the 4th that Zhu Shunqing of the detective team returned to Changshu from Shanghai and learned of the incident. He immediately reported to Director Yin of the Public Security Bureau, who that night sent inspector Cheng Bin to the countryside for a secret investigation, and also sent inspector Chen Pinquan to supervise. They obtained some clues and searched the homes of the opium robbers Qian Beilin, Shi Heshang, and Wang Gengsong, but found that they had abandoned their homes and fled. Only Shi Pangshi, the wife of Shi Heshang, was taken to the bureau for investigation. Later, it was said that the main culprits had fled to Xieqiao, or were hiding in Xingfu and other places. The Public Security Bureau sent police officers to investigate and arrest them, but without success. The Public Security Bureau then sent inspector Cheng and detective team leader Zhu Shunqing and others, leading a team to the countryside to investigate and arrest them strictly. After two days, there was no result. Only a large amount of rice, yellow beans, and other items were found in Qian Linlin's house. Until the evening of the 7th, a secret agent reported that Qian Linlin was hiding at the home of a relative surnamed Yao in Cui Jia Xiaoqiao. They then went with the 10th resident station of the district. It was already around 2:00 AM. When they arrived at the place, they saw a figure speeding away. The police ordered them to stop, but the person continued to move forward. The police fired a shot from their box gun, and the person stopped. They went forward and arrested the person, who turned out to be Qian Linlin, the main culprit of the robbery. When asked where the soil was hidden, he said it was in his father Yao Nannan's pig shed. The police went to investigate, but Yao Nannan had already fled after receiving the news. In the pig shed in his home, they found a large quantity of opium, which was loaded into sacks and baskets by the police, and Qian Linlin was taken back to the resident station. At 5:00 AM the next morning, he was transferred to the Public Security General Bureau in the city. Inspector Cheng and others separately reported the investigation to Director Yin. At about 9:00 AM, Director Yin invited Secretary Jin of the County Government, Supervisory Committee member Shi Minyong of the County Party Department, and members of the Rejection Society to the bureau to inspect and weigh the items in detail. In total, there were 127 packages of Sichuan-Yunnan soil, weighing 357 catties and eight and a half taels. The director then personally affixed the seal of the Public Security Bureau and sealed them together. In the afternoon, Lu Zhibin, the head of the third section, interrogated the prisoners separately. According to Qian Linlin, he is from this county and has been working as a car driver in Shanghai, Zhejiang and other places for 12 years. He is currently driving at Guanghua University in Shanghai. This time, he returned to Changshu for some matters. As for the soil robbery, there was a Jiangyin friend surnamed Zhu, whose name he did not know. He often stays in Shanghai, and when he comes to Changshu, he often goes to the Zhang family at No. 38 behind the Shui Xian Temple outside the South Gate. I am not very close to him. He once came to my house for a meal last year. The day before yesterday, the Zhu surname came to Dayi Bridge again and saw me. At that time, I did not talk about the soil. Until the afternoon of the 2nd, I was about to go to the city when the Zhu surname called me to go up to the teahouse and he said to me, today three sand boats are passing by, I want to ask you to call a few people to help. I went to call Shi Heshang, Wang Gengsong, Wang Binggen, and others. Near the evening, I saw a sand boat passing by, and later two more boats passed by. Zhu jumped onto a boat with us, went to the sand boat at the ferry at the end of the market, and transported their soil here. The pistol was not held by me. Later, the sand boat left, and we also rocked to another place. At that time, I saw these things, and I dared not report it. I was afraid and fled. As for Zhu, I don't know where he went. The rice and beans were half deposited in my house by the bean curd shop, and half were my own. When asked about Shi Pangshi, she said that her husband, Shi Heshang, was a farmer by trade, and did not know about the soil robbery. Later, the Public Security Bureau temporarily detained Qian and others in the bureau, and prepared a document together with the opium and the prisoners to be sent to the county judiciary for review. The ten resident stations of Qian Linlin's family's rice and beans are guarded by police.

Yangzhou

The Honghu Steamboat Was Robbed: The Honghu steamboat of the Yongxing Company of Shaobo, which runs the Xing Shao route, departed from Shao at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday, carrying a total of seven passengers. At 8:00 PM that night, while traveling through Qizhuang, more than ten miles from Chuanchuan, seven bandits were seen on both sides of the bank, carrying box cannons. They fired at the boat and ordered it to stop. The driver knew there was a bandit alert and could not resist, so he docked the boat on the shore. The bandits then boarded the boat from the tugboat and searched it, taking away about 200 yuan in cash, jewelry, clothes, and other items. They also shot and injured an old man in the fire cabin and two passengers. The boat has now returned to Shaobu, and the injured have been taken to the Yian Hospital for treatment. It is reported that the old man has not yet had the bullet removed and has been sent to Laiyang for treatment.

The Process of Surrendering Weapons by the Xinzhen Business Corps: Regarding the dispatch of a team from the Yangzhou garrison to Xian to collect the guns of the town's business corps, it is now known that at 10:00 AM on the 7th, Shao Xiao Zhang Yuan, sent by the Superintendent, and Li Qinhu, commander of the 94th Brigade, led a team of soldiers. Under the secret order of the Superintendent, they went to Xian to meet with Wu, the captain of the 23rd team of the 6th District of the Water Public Security Bureau, and together with Zhang Wen, the director of the 4th Branch of the Public Security Bureau, led the police to the residence of the business corps. They collected more than a dozen long and short guns and arrested Wang Changfa, the platoon leader of the corps, and sent him to the military law office of the Superintendent for interrogation. Tao, the captain of the corps, knew the wind and avoided the situation afterward.

Four Banks Merchants Petition to Maintain Introduction Tickets: The Hunan, Hubei, West Anhui and Anhui Four Banks Grain Merchants Federation petitioned the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Salt Administration, and the Central Political Committee in response to the Legislative Yuan's resolution to abolish introduction tickets and collect taxes on the spot, appealing to maintain introduction tickets to maintain their livelihoods. The content generally states that the introduction ticket was created in the late Qing Dynasty. At that time, each ticket merchant reported to the public in advance 12,000 taels of silver, and the government issued a license allowing them to forever handle transportation. After the restoration, the Qing system was still followed. Last year, the registration fee for ticket inspection was set, and the ticket merchants paid 4 million oceans, allowing them to remain the same. Now, the salt tax law reported in the Legislative Yuan states that salt is freely traded by the people, and the introduction merchant system will cease from the date of publication of the public notice. This is to implement on-site tax collection. When the news came, the ticket merchants were panicked, and various industries moved, fearing that once published, those who would cut off their livelihood would be more than millions of households. The introduction merchant system was a monopoly in the Qing Dynasty, but it has been transferred and has become a kind of reserve certificate. Many widows and orphans use it for their livelihood. Abolishing the introduction bank is tantamount to announcing the death penalty to millions of households.

Gaoyou

The High Court Sends a Committee to Thoroughly Investigate the Black幕 of the Prison: A citizen of this county, so and so, filed a complaint with the Suzhou Higher Court about various black幕 of the prison and attached multiple copies of the local Huaihai Daily newspaper that published the news. Now the court has sent Fu Runlai, the alternate magistrate of Jiangdu County Court, to thoroughly investigate. Magistrate Fu arrived in You this morning (8th) and immediately went to the county government to meet with County Magistrate Wang to discuss everything. He used a business card to send someone to invite Shi Wenjun, the manager of the Huaihai Daily newspaper, to the county government. He also summoned the prison guard captain and more than ten prisoners. Magistrate Fu opened the court, asked a few questions, and asked Mr. Shi to present several pieces of evidence of the black幕 of the prison in court. After the inquiry, he ordered everyone to sign the record. It is reported that Mr. Fu will return to Yangzhou tonight to report the truth to his superiors.

Two Robbery Felons are Executed by Firing Squad: Xu Kui, a detective of the 6th District of the Gaoyou Water Provincial Public Security Team, previously captured two robbery felons, Zhu Jihuai and Zhang Xiqing, in Qingjiang. They were immediately sent to the Yangzhou Pacification Superintendent's Office for interrogation. After several interrogations by the superintendent's office, they both admitted to robbing the Xifeng and Hengfeng small steamships of the Litong Company at the Qilizha place in Baoying County. Now the Superintendent's Office has sent the criminals back to the 6th District Department of Gaoyou to be escorted to the location of the incident for execution by firing squad. After receiving the order, District Chief Cheng immediately ordered the team to escort the two criminals to Qilizha for execution on the morning of the 7th.

The Chenghuang Temple Will Begin Restoration: Secretary Qiang and Section Chief Cai, representatives of the County Government, Renhou, Renhai, and Miaolang, representatives of the Buddhist Association, Chen Ru, representative of the Chamber of Commerce, two Taoist grandmothers Weng and Wang, and Ji Tiankai, representative of the Chenghuang Temple Taoists, discussed for a long time in the Chenghuang Temple at 10:00 AM on the 7th. All representatives made a public decision on erecting a statue of the Premier or enshrining a memorial tablet of the Premier in the temple. It is reported that the Taoist grandmothers have hired many carpenters and painters and will begin work this afternoon to restore the old idols. The rest will be gradually restored. All expenses will be raised by the Taoist grandmothers. Later, because they did not obtain the authorities' permission, the Taoist grandmothers ordered the craftsmen to stop work and went to the county government this morning to request the posting of a restoration announcement. It is still unknown how it will be resolved.

Qingjiang

The Theater Bandit Was Captured and Sent to the County: Zhu Zhenhe, a theater bandit from Huaiyin, went to Siyang last autumn, gathered a large number of bandits, harassed Huai, and occupied Sanke Tree Market. He burned and robbed Linqiao, Wangwei, Wangjia Caomiao, Yuanji, Langshi and other places. Because the large bandits scattered and could not survive, he sneaked back to Sanke Tree Market to hide. The incident was discovered by Deng Jianli, the captain of the Second Squadron of the local police, who secretly ordered Zhang Aizhou, the captain of the Third Platoon of the team, to capture him and send him to the headquarters of the squadron. According to the interrogation, he admitted to being a bandit. On the 6th, Squadron Captain Deng sent the bandit to the headquarters of the battalion and transferred to the county.

County Magistrate Wen's Plan to Break Down Opium Dens: There are many opium dens in Siyang County, especially the Haiwu opium den in the west gate, which has many customers. County Magistrate Wen, according to a secret report, specially disguised himself as a merchant and went to the Hai opium den in the west of the city to buy opium. Hai did not suspect that he was the county magistrate, and invited Wen to a secret room, took out opium lamps and opium guns. Wen went out and called people in and took Hai Wu and the opium together, causing other opium dens not to dare to turn on the lights for a while.

Nantong

Remaining Bandit Chiefs Sentenced to Death: Fang Zanqing and Xue Xien, the remaining bandit chiefs from Tongyi Yudong, gathered crowds to rob and kill people. After being captured by the police team, they were sent to Nantong County Court for trial. The trial was concluded and sentenced on the 9th. Both bandits were sentenced to death.

Held a Party-Government Talk Conference: Representatives of various party and government agencies in this county held a party-government talk conference at the county government on the 9th. The following important cases were resolved: (1) Zhang Jian's confiscated property, 40% of which belongs to the county, will be used for local education and relief undertakings; (2) urging all districts to form agricultural and educational associations within a time limit; (3) the county government will send personnel to investigate the surrender of the Communist Party in Yiyu and other districts; (4) the county's scout troops will hold a joint camp next month.

The Court Recovers Embezzled Funds from the Detention Center: Hu Xianzou, the director of the detention center, was dismissed after the High Court found that he had embezzled public funds. Yuan Wenbo, the director of the Qidong detention center, took over. For the sake of prudence, the Nantong Court ordered Hu Xianzou to hand over his duties first on the 9th and sent the clerk Gu Guangyuan as an agent. When Yuan arrived in Tong and took over, Hu embezzled public funds and must hand them over immediately. If he violated, he would be detained. All books and accounts were collected for investigation. After Hu handed over his duties, he was monitored in the court.

Jiaxing

County Education Association Elects Executives: The Jiaxing District Education Associations have been appointed by the County Executive Committee to reorganize and guide them. They have already held an inaugural meeting. On the afternoon of the 9th, they held a re-election of executives of the County Education Association in the auditorium of the County Party Department. As a result of the election, Chen Jingbo, Yuan Wenxiong, Yao Baoyan, Niu Chengqi, Qian Qi, Ma Shuzi, Wang Chunong and other seven people were elected as executives, and Shen Dazan was elected as provincial representative.

County Government County Administration Meeting: The Jiaxing County Government held its 41st county administration meeting yesterday. A proposal was made to increase the collection of public funds for various police donations. It was resolved that for donations for shops and houses within 1,000 yuan, the public and finance bureaus would each divide the money equally. For those exceeding 1,000 yuan, the old plan would still be followed.

Hangzhou

Construction Hall Plans to Allocate Funds for the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Project: It is reported that the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway project is expected to be opened to traffic as early as May. It is reported that the construction funds for the project have not yet been established with the Shanghai Silver Group loan, so it cannot be used for the required funds. The Construction Hall has found another way, and has overdrafted 200,000 from the Bank of China, 50,000 from the Agricultural and Industrial Bank, and allocated 50,000 from the Financial Hall. A total of 300,000 yuan has been allocated successively. The project is still proceeding as usual and construction continues.

Coalfield Reserves in Zhejiang Province: Although Zhejiang Province is a region of water conservancy, Tianmu and Xianxia divide the northwest. According to the estimation of mining scholars, the amount of coalfield reserves is quite astonishing: (1) The Changxing coalfield covers 400,000 square kilometers, from Daodui Mountain in the east, Niutou Mountain in the south, Guangde in the west, and Zhangjiakou in the north, producing 40 million tons of coal. (2) The Hepingzhen coalfield has very thick coal seams, with the ground surface at about 1,000 meters, with a reserve of 20 million tons. The coalfield outcrops in the nearby valleys are estimated to be more than 1 million tons. (3) The Wuxing Hengshanqiao coalfield also covers 14 square kilometers, containing 40 million tons of coal, and is easy to mine, and the coal seam is also good. It is reported that some merchants will form a large-scale company to mine it.

Ningbo

The Progress of the Naval Academy: The Ministry of the Navy recently plans to build a large-scale naval academy in Xiangshan Port. The site area was surveyed and determined by Chen Shaokuan, acting Minister of the Ministry. The surrounding area is about 300 mu. The Naval Special Service Battalion stationed in Xiangshan is engaged in the foundation work of the school and will complete it in a few days, and then begin to build the school buildings. It is reported that the school's recurring expenses have been set at 30,000 yuan per month. Captain Wang of the Hai Rong warship and Captain Gao of the Tongji warship have been appointed by the Ministry to be responsible for the naval school plan and engineering, and to supervise the progress at any time.

Twelve Bandits Sent to the Province for Review: The Zhenhai Overseas Marine Police Department recently captured Ye Mianxiu, Chen Zuning, Zhang Laowu, Li Xiaying, Peng Xianwang, Shao Laowu, Chen Asi, Hong Liangqing, Li Dazhong, Pan Naier, Yu Asan, and Chen Xianbiao on the Guangji ship by the Wen Chaowu warship stationed in Wen. Yesterday, the provincial order was issued to send all the captured bandits to the province for trial. After receiving the order, the bureau prepared a document and sent it to the county government for transfer to the provincial government.

First Day of Shaanxi Education Bureau Directors Conference

▲Opening Ceremony Held at 10 AM

▲More Than 300 Members and Guests Attended

(Xi'an Quick Telegram) The first Shaanxi Provincial Education Bureau Directors Conference was held at 10 AM on the 3rd of this month. The venue was set up in the auditorium of the Department of Education. More than 60 members attended, and the Department of Education assigned 8 members to attend. The chairman of the conference was Li Fanyi, Director of the Department of Education, and the secretary-general of the conference was Yin Guoyong. The guests included Chairman Yang of the Provincial Government, Zhang Mingjing, member of the Party Department, Li Zhigang, Director of the Department of Finance, Li Bailing, member of the Provincial Government, Nan Ruji, Secretary-General, Yu Jun, President of the High Court, Sun Weiru, Commander of the 17th Division, Ma Qingyuan, Commander of the Garrison, as well as representatives from various agencies and schools, and 200 people from the educational circles in the provincial capital.
