Report on Innovation Work of the Ministry of Education

▲February

The Ministry of Education recently submitted the report on innovation work for February of the 20th year to the Executive Yuan for record. The original text is as follows:

(1) Higher Education

(1) Reorganization and closure of public and private universities: Instructions were issued to comply with the regulations on reorganizing Peking University, Peking Normal University, and National Peking University. An order was issued to close the private Nanyang Medical College, instructing the Shanghai Education Bureau to consult with the Medical College of National Central University to screen the students of the college. (2) Investigation of the general situation of schools above the junior college level since the 18th year: A general situation survey form for the 18th year was created and sent to all universities and junior colleges for completion and return. (3) Regulations stipulating matters that should be paid attention to in the operation of universities were issued for compliance: Based on the survey, the most urgent matters for improvement in universities are approximately the following: 1. Enrich equipment and content. 2. Restrict teachers from taking on concurrent teaching positions. 3. Monitor student absenteeism. 4. Clearly define examination methods. 5. Seriously reorganize dormitories. A general order was issued for universal attention to these matters as the priority for all improvements. (4) Issuance of study abroad certificates: Approval was granted for the issuance of public-funded study abroad certificates for a total of one person (one to the UK). Approval was granted for the issuance of self-funded study abroad certificates for a total of forty-seven people (four to the UK, one to the US, four to Germany, four to France, six to Belgium, and twenty-eight to Japan).

(2) Secondary Education

(1) A list of secondary schools approved by the Ministry in February: Juxin Junior High School in Changde, Hunan; Sino-Japanese Middle School in Tianjin, Hebei; Changjing Junior High School in Jiangyin, Jiangsu. (2) A list of secondary school board of directors approved in February: The board of directors of the Private Anqing Junior High School in Anqing, Anhui; the board of directors of the Private Tongkou Middle School in Anxin, Hebei. (3) Compilation of a list of private secondary schools filed with the Ministry (from the 17th year to January of the 20th year) and a list of boards of directors. (4) Promulgation of curriculum standards for senior high school normal programs.

(3) Elementary Education

(1) Drafting of measures to promote elementary education in prosperous cities. (2) Drafting of measures to ensure sufficient enrollment of children in rural elementary schools. (3) Drafting of measures for elementary school graduation examinations. (4) A letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs sending the book "Mongolian Suli and its Education" to be forwarded to Dr. Mongolian Suli, and requesting that the recent situation of kindergarten and lower elementary education in our country be conveyed.

(4) Overseas Chinese Education

(1) A list of overseas Chinese schools registered in February: Yuzhi School in Penang; Tokyo Overseas Chinese Elementary School in Tokyo, Japan. (2) A letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs requesting commendation of the consul stationed in Yangon. (3) Promulgation of regulations for overseas Chinese elementary and secondary schools.

(5) Local Education Administrative Matters

(1) An order to the Guangdong Provincial Department of Education instructing them to report the names and financial status of all public and private middle schools under the jurisdiction of the counties in the province to the Ministry. (2) An instruction to retain Huang Shiheng as the Director of the Hunan Provincial Department of Education.

(6) Social Education

(1) A report to the Executive Yuan requesting the Xinjiang Provincial Government to allow members of the Northwest Scientific Expedition to pass without obstruction. (2) A telegram on behalf of the Peiping Municipal Government transferring one ancient cannon each engraved with the characters "Wu Sangui" and "Chen Guodong" to be displayed at the Nanjing Antiquities Preservation Institute. (3) Guo Lianfeng, Shi Wei, and Wang Lun were assigned to take over the Minglun Hall from the Capital Garrison Headquarters, and a letter was sent to the Adjutant Office of the Headquarters requesting the issuance of a notice that no troops were allowed to occupy it. (4) The Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education jointly issued an abstract of the National Calendar for the 21st year. (5) Peng Baichuan, Feng Chenglin, Wang Depu, and Wang Xuesu were appointed as members of the Film Censorship Committee, and the Ministry of Interior was notified to investigate and appoint three people to establish the Film Censorship Committee. (6) A general order was issued to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities to follow the attached form to report the social sports matters that should be reported within the time limit and to supplement the previous situation. (7) A table of the phonetic symbols for the 20th year was sent to various agencies in the capital. (8) (Advertisements were placed in party newspapers in Beijing and Shanghai)

Announcing the collection of lyrics for the National Games. (9) The Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education jointly submitted to the Executive Yuan whether the seal of the Film Censorship Committee should be submitted to the National Government for verification and issuance, or whether it should be published by the Ministry. Request for verification and implementation. (10) The deadline for the collection of national anthems was extended, totaling 1,572 entries, which have been jointly preliminarily reviewed.

(7) Mongolian and Tibetan Education

(1) Promotion of phonetic symbols: A general order was issued to all banners of Mongolia and Tibet to immediately select personnel to go to the phonetic symbol training classes sponsored by the educational administrative agencies of neighboring provinces and cities. After completing the training, they should return to their original places of assignment to teach and promote them. (2) Cultivation of teachers: A reply was sent to the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission regarding the revised organizational outline of the Kang Tibetan Teacher Training Institute attached to the Third Middle School of Yunnan Province for review. (3) Revision of the budget for Mongolian and Tibetan schools in Nanjing and Kangding: A letter was sent to the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission stating that the budget for Mongolian and Tibetan schools in Nanjing and Kangding was not in compliance with the trial budget regulations for the 19th year promulgated by the government, and requested that it be corrected according to the regulations and four additional copies be sent to the Ministry for joint submission.

(8) Implementation, Review, and Interpretation of Educational Laws and Regulations (1) The Executive Yuan ordered the promulgation of 18 types of laws and regulations, including the Education Association Law, the Regulations on Reviewing Party Doctrine Teachers, and the Examination Regulations. (2) Approval was given to the Central Training Department to issue instructions on guiding the reorganization and organization methods of the Education Association. (3) Promulgation of the Provisional Regulations of the Overseas Chinese Education Association. (4) Promulgation of the Rules of the Provisional Management Committee Office of the Private China Public School. (5) A telegram was sent to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities instructing them that when higher-level education associations hold membership congresses, representatives should be elected by the membership congresses of lower-level education associations to attend, with two representatives from each district and one from each county or city. The term of office is temporarily set at one year. In addition to the attending representatives, all other members of the Education Association have the right to be elected as directors, supervisors, and executive officers. (6) An instruction was given to the Shaanxi Provincial Department of Education to inform principals and teachers that they are not listed as civil servants. The head of the county education bureau is an appointed official and should be subject to screening and review. Whether other positions such as supervisors need to be subject to screening and review should be determined based on the organizational regulations. (7) An instruction was given to the Henan Provincial Department of Education to inform them that it is not necessary to set additional restrictions on the marriage age of middle school students outside of the Civil Code. Teachers and staff of each school should provide kind and earnest guidance at any time to make students regard early marriage as a taboo. (8) A telegram was sent on behalf of the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities instructing the county and city education associations to allow the executive officers to mutually elect one person as the standing executive officer. (9) An instruction was given to the supervisor of students studying in Japan to inform them that, upon the approval of the Executive Yuan, female students who marry men from other provinces may continue to receive their original public funds or subsidies from the provinces from which they originally received them, unless the laws and regulations of those provinces provide otherwise, until the central government has such regulations. (10) A review was conducted of a total of eight sets of separate laws and regulations from various provinces and cities.

(9) Commendation for Donating Funds for Education

(1) A report was submitted to the Executive Yuan stating that the Wuxi Yizhuang donated more than 100,000 yuan for education, requesting verification and forwarding to the National Government for a clear order of commendation. (2) Three first-class certificates of commendation were issued for donating funds for education, four second-class certificates, and two third-class certificates. (10) Education Statistics

(1) An instruction was issued to the education departments and bureaus of all provinces and cities to forward the survey form for primary education administrative personnel, instructing them to fill it out in compliance and to instruct the county education bureaus to fill it out as well. (2) An instruction was issued to all provincial and private universities to re-issue the university student survey form, instructing them to fill it out within one week. (3) A letter was sent to various agencies in Beijing and embassies in Europe and the United States to send the survey form for students studying abroad, requesting that they be instructed to fill it out. (4) A survey form for students studying abroad was drafted. (5) Statistical charts for social education in the 17th year were revised. (6) The student survey forms for Henan University, Lanzhou Zhongshan University, Changwu China University, Peiping University College of Engineering, Women's Normal College, and Peiyang Institute of Technology were categorized and filled out.

(11) Review of Educational Books

(1) Textbook approved for review: "New Textbook of National Language Phonetic Symbols," compiled by Jiang Jingfu, for use in schools at all levels, published by Zhonghua Book Company, reviewed on February 18th of the 20th year. (2) Textbooks approved for publication: "History of Imperialist Aggression Against China," Chen Binhe, World Book Company; "Unequal Treaties of Various Countries with China," Cheng Zhonghang, World Book Company; "History of Japanese Aggression Against Manchuria and Mongolia," You Henggui, World Book Company; "Elementary English Grammar," Liu Chongqiu, Zhonghua Book Company; "Kindergarten Reader," Shen Baiying, Commercial Press; "English Literature Reader," Lin Yutang, Kaiming Bookstore; "Literary English Reader," Wang Chonghui, Zhonghua Book Company; "How Humans Conquer Nature," translated by Chen Jingying, Commercial Press; "Human Food," translated by He Qikuan, Commercial Press; "Early Seaside People," translated by He Qikuan, Commercial Press; "Ancient Humans," translated by Chen Shuliang, Commercial Press; "Later Cave Dwellers," translated by He Qikuan, Commercial Press; "Eskimos," translated by He Qikuan, Commercial Press; "Collection of Children's Songs," Ma Rongtan, Commercial Press.

Yang Lianggong, President of Anhui University, Resigns

Yang Lianggong, the president of Anhui University, has only been in office for two semesters. Recently, there have been repeated disturbances, making it difficult to maintain order. Yesterday, Yang submitted his resignation to the provincial government. The main points of Yang's resignation first stated his contributions to the university, then discussed the occurrence of the disturbances, and included the statement that "students are acting wantonly and violently, and administrative laws are almost simultaneously losing their effectiveness."

Local News

Various Schools Commemorate Martyrs Who Died in the Campaign Against the Rebels

▲ Jinan University: National Jinan University held a memorial service for the martyrs who died in the campaign against the rebels in the auditorium at 9:00 a.m. yesterday. More than a thousand teachers and students attended. The service was presided over by Dean of Students Tang Demin, who reported the four purposes of the meeting: (1) This year, industry and commerce have gradually returned to their original state, politics has gradually gotten on track, and the majority of the people have been able to live and work in peace and contentment. This is all the price paid by the soldiers at the front who fought for the country and quelled the rebellion, regardless of their own safety. (2) Any country in the midst of a great revolution must rely on the sacrifice of countless soldiers before the national policy can be determined. The United States and France are examples of this. (3) After the European War, tens of thousands of ladies paid their respects and shed tears at the Tomb of the Unknown Soldier in Europe on Memorial Day. This is because, after the pain subsided, they admired the unnamed soldiers who sacrificed for the nation and for peace. Their emotions are the same as our emotions when we should commemorate the soldiers who sacrificed for the unification and peace of the Chinese nation. In the future, the country will become more prosperous, and the people will enjoy the happiness bestowed by peace and progress. However, these soldiers who sacrificed for the country will no longer be mentioned in five or ten years. What are our feelings? (4) The Chinese nation has a deeply rooted love for peace, so opposition to war was the common view of the general public in the past. However, to eliminate war, there must be the strength to eliminate war. The martyrs who died in battle are loyal and brave men who would rather sacrifice their personal happiness, family, and life to eliminate the rebellion and achieve peace, and to create happiness for the new China. We must know that sacrificing oneself for the independence of the nation and the peaceful unification of the country is the greatest and most glorious thing. The martyrs who died in battle are truly our role models. Following this, Zhan Kui, Deputy Chairman of the University Affairs Council and Director of the Middle School Department, gave a speech, saying that the thorns in the future of the country have already been cleared by the martyrs who died in battle. In the future, the construction of all things must rely on the succession and efforts of young students. If they cannot bear the mission of construction, then they are all sinners against the fallen martyrs.

▲ Labor University: National Labor University, on March 10th, following an order from the Ministry of Education, held a memorial service for the martyrs of the army, navy, and air force who died in the campaign against the rebels. At 8:00 a.m. that morning, President Wang Jingqi led the faculty, staff, and students, all wearing black gauze armbands, to gather in the auditorium to hold the meeting as scheduled. President Wang served as the chief celebrant, and after the ceremony, he delivered a speech with extremely mournful words. The entire venue was solemn, and the music of mourning especially increased the tragic atmosphere. A funeral couplet was hung in front of the stage, reading: "The soldiers fought bravely, sharing the same hatred, vowing to kill the chief culprit. The eternal national殇 becomes a pain." "The red blood is mottled, in the nine heavens and nine earths, summoning the souls of many soldiers. The Yangtze River flows, sobbing with lingering sorrow." The memorial text and speech are omitted.

▲ Nanyang Advanced Commercial School: Nanyang Advanced Commercial School on Tiantong'an Tongji Road held a memorial service for the martyrs who died in battle in the auditorium yesterday morning. All faculty, staff, and male and female students attended. The ceremony was held as scheduled. Acting Principal Wang Buxian reported the purpose of the memorial service. Free Talk

World Anecdotes

— Hai Ke

▲The British surgeon Sir J. Cantlie knows an old lady of seventy years. It is said that her grandfather was seventy years old when he had his first son. Later, this son also had a daughter at the age of seventy. To be able to have children at the advanced age of seventy is also a rare record.

▲In Java, only the gentry can own land freely. Europeans can only lease from them for a term of seventy-five years and must provide half of the land to the gentry for free rice cultivation.

▲A new school of marriage has been established in the United States. All unmarried men and women can enroll in the school. The founder is a lady who says that 90 percent of marital unhappiness is caused by the couple's inability to understand each other.

▲There is a fish market in London called Billingsgate. All fish transactions are completed here. The market has been in existence for a thousand years.

▲There is a photograph in the United States that is ten feet long and ninety-six feet wide. It cost thirty pounds sterling to produce. This is the largest photograph in the world.

▲There is a strange profession in England in which people specialize in searching for research materials in museums. If someone has scientific questions and goes to the museum to study, this person helps them search for materials and charges a corresponding fee for a living. However, there are fewer and fewer people doing this job lately.

▲A professor at the University of New New South Bottom in the United States said that music can be used as an aid when a patient cannot fall asleep due to a disease curable by science. It is very effective.

Recording the Wrongful Deaths of Two Women

— Jie Lu

There are many people in the world who die unjustly. All epidemic and acute diseases have a way to be cured. However, due to the lack of attention to hygiene among the people and the lack of knowledge of medicine, an unknown number of people die unnaturally every year. A Mr. So-and-so from the West once wrote a paper on "True Death and Apparent Death," which gave many examples. It roughly stated that claw marks and disordered bones are often found in coffins. This is a clear sign of resurrection after apparent death. Therefore, if the body is not buried until twenty-four hours after death, it is often difficult to avoid the tragedy of being buried alive. This is not an ideal talk, it is actually very common. According to what I have heard, two women clearly died unjustly. I record them as a warning to others.

The wife of a neighbor, Yu, is very virtuous and loved by her in-laws. Her husband is a merchant in Hanzhong. She returned to her hometown to live during her pregnancy. The woman suffered from hemorrhoids and was in great pain when they flared up. Someone told her to apply borneol and honey to the anus, which would cure it immediately. The woman applied it as instructed. Unexpectedly, the baby could not stand the smell of borneol and suddenly surged upward, and the woman died. Her husband heard the news and returned home, weeping bitterly over the coffin, not wanting to live. Those who saw it shed tears for her. Isn't this a case of wrongful death due to a lack of medical knowledge? Those who abuse potent drugs should be warned.

The other day, there was a woman named A Ying on the street. She was twenty-three years old. She was still washing clothes in the river after breakfast. At dusk, she died of abdominal pain. I heard people talking about it and asked if she had any other illnesses. They replied that she only had abdominal pain from morning to night. I was afraid that an epidemic might break out in our town, so I didn't want to go to see her. Later, after detailed investigation, I learned that A Ying was from Fenghua and lived in our town. Because her husband was as useless as the second in the proverb, she had many lovers. One night, she had an affair with someone named Jia on the ground of a ruined temple and fled when she was seen. I then realized that this must have been typhoid fever that caused her death. It is a pity that I did not know the truth at the time, and A Ying's husband was as foolish as a deer or pig. The neighbors all avoided him as if he were a plague. Therefore, a romantic ghost was added to the city of wrongful deaths. Having witnessed these two events, I feel very sad. Regardless of my humble abilities, I took up my pen to record them as above.

Words of Heartbreak

— Someone

Mr. Ye Chengzhong's descendant, Zhongfang, is intelligent and outstanding, but unrestrained and unruly. He is known in Shanghai for his petty troubles. Recently, I don't know what major stimulation he received, but he left home and went elsewhere. Before leaving, he sent a letter to his beloved, Shirley, saying, "Now, as you wish, I have left home and ran away. The future is vast and I don't know where I will end up. Recalling the scenery of this day last year, who would have expected the sadness of this moment this year. Although Zhong has a heart, what can he do if you don't care. Zhong is leaving now. I hope you take care." Unexpectedly, this gentleman is also burdened by love. Reading his letter, although only a few words, the heartbreak is extreme. I wonder if that Shirley was also moved by it.

A Record of Visiting the "President Madison" by Various Universities

— Cheng Zhizheng

The American Dollar Steamship Company has recently promoted its business and contacted the national sentiment. It specifically invited students from various universities to visit the "President Madison" on the sixth of this month through the YMCA. One hundred and fifty-one professors and students from various universities arrived. They departed at 2 PM and returned at 5 PM. There were many noteworthy things during this time, so I will describe one or two of them as follows.

▲Tension in the Air at the New Customs Wharf: When the company initially invited students from various universities, it was not limited to graduating classes. Later, the number of applicants increased dramatically. Taking Jiaotong University as an example, there were already 150 people. Subsequently, the company felt that the number of people was too large and decided to receive them in stages, first accommodating the senior students. These people will be graduating soon and are more concerned about the issue of going abroad. For a time, the new customs wharf was filled with candidate bachelors. Nine out of ten were wearing suits, laughing and talking, and the atmosphere gradually became tense.

▲No Space to Stand on the Ferry: The invitation from the company stated that they would meet at 1:50 PM. By 1:50 PM, the small ferry for receiving guests from the Dollar Company slowly arrived. It can be said that they kept their word. The boat was huge, but there was no space to stand up or down due to the large number of passengers. People in the company told each other that this was an unprecedented record for congestion. As the guests boarded the boat, it immediately set sail. At that time, more than ten people from Daxia University arrived by car and rushed to the wharf, but it was too late. All of them looked disappointed.

▲Welcoming Guests to Tour Freely: After arriving in Pudong, the "President Madison" was already in sight. The company staff respectfully invited the guests to board the boat and rest in the lounge. The arrangement of the ship was as luxurious as a first-class hotel in Shanghai, and it was even cleaner and more solemn. After entering the room, each person was given a piece of paper, instructed to write their name and school on it, and then put it on their lapel for identification. All parts of the ship were open, even the driver's room, where tourists were stopped, could be introduced and explained by a mechanic.

▲More Than Two Thousand Yuan for a Trip to the United States: The area of the ship is extremely large. It is divided into bedrooms, dance halls, dining rooms, writing rooms, and social rooms, all of which are extremely luxurious and look like a heavenly residence. The first-class room has two beds in the middle, and all other necessary items are available. When asked about the price to the United States, they said it required more than 480 US dollars, which is more than 2,000 Chinese dollars.

▲Tea and Snacks Fill the Room with Spring: At four o'clock, the crew invited all visitors to the dining room for tea. Although there were many people, the restaurant was quite large, so it was not too crowded. There were six people at each table, with two plates of pastries and toast. The hospitality can be said to be thoughtful. After the meal, the group went to the social room, where the YMCA representative, Mr. Haimuhua, gave a speech. He said that he was also a Chinese student. He was born in Suzhou, went to the United States for schooling when he grew up, and then returned to China. He then thanked the company for their hospitality. He occasionally mixed Suzhou dialect in his speech, which made the audience burst into laughter.

▲Distributing Books and Saying Goodbye: The ship has many printed items. I was given more than thirty books by the company staff. Others also received several books each. Many of them are expensive photographs. The cost of printing is not small. The company's ability to attract customers can be seen from this. At five o'clock, we left the ship and said goodbye to the host.

▲Returning with the Waves, Also Students Abroad: On the way back, the students from each school told each other about the joy of this trip and said, "From now on, we are also students abroad." Mr. Haimuhua expressed his willingness to sincerely assist students from various universities in going abroad and planned to set up a discussion group so that students can participate together and study everything.

A Record of the Crystal Mine Near Zhu Township

— Wang Ri Sou

Yesterday, my friend Zhang came from Fuzhou and told me about the mining of crystal in the near Zhu Township of Mawei, which can be used as a topic of conversation. I will record it here to make the "Free Talk" real.

▲Finding a Mine While Building a Tomb: There is a mountain in the near Zhu Township of Mawei. It is said that there are many crystals in it, so it is named Crystal Mountain. However, the crystals are all deeply buried in the mountain. The mountain is big, so there is no way to mine it. Recently, a villager named Ren built a tomb for his ancestors, so he hired many workers to cultivate the cemetery he bought on Crystal Mountain. When they dug to eight or nine feet, they found many white stones. A worker with experience said that there must be crystals below. At that time, the owner did not know about it, so they warned each other not to reveal it.

▲Mining at Night: That night, the workers took advantage of the owner's ignorance and mined all night. At about three feet, they found many crystals. The matter was known to the villagers, and they came to negotiate. The workers said that the crystals were obtained by their own blood and sweat and should belong to them. However, the villager named Ren said that the land belonged to him and he must take back the crystals. The two sides were stubborn and almost came to blows. After mediation, they each divided half. At that time, they thought it was a rare commodity and refused to sell it. Later, because there was no place to sell it, they were willing to sell it at a low price. Mr. Zhang once bought a crystal for two gold coins.

▲Shape of the Crystal: Each crystal is as big as a Western melon, but the shape is a geometric polyhedron. The outside stone is white and not transparent. Mr. Zhang once broke a corner of it and realized that the inside was all transparent black crystal. The outer wrapping is only a very thick white stone skin. Some say that the crystal is all transparent and has no stone skin wrapping it. But then, this kind of crystal is not yet fully mature, or it is another kind of mineral.

Jia'an's Fleeing from Painting

— Zheng Yimei

Among paintings, flowers and plants are more difficult than landscapes and figures. The swing of the brush spontaneously has a spiritual appeal; each painting has its own color and fragrance. Otherwise, it can easily become broken branches or become too coarse and extensive. If the artist attempts to produce juxtaposed dense buds it becomes cumbersome and stagnant, and difficult to please. Among contemporary flower painters, Mr. Chen Zhemian of Haiyu is considered a giant. Mr. Chen lived in Wuzhong, near Yinmaqiao, and made a living by selling paintings. He was able to paint landscapes, figures, insects, fish, birds, and animals. He also wrote flowers and plants, which were light, graceful, and elegant. Without a model or draft, the stroke would follow his will, and have its own style. Those who sought a small picture or a large scroll would wear the threshold through. Mr. Chen would paint all year round, but still accumulate works like a mountain, and it was difficult to make up for the backlog. Mr. Chen also socialized widely, and friends came to chat. He was even more distracted by the art of painting. Unable to help himself, he would pack his painting equipment and escape to the Canglang Pavilion. He would mix lead and pigments and bury himself in his work. When sunset came, he would leisurely return, and even his family would not know where he came from. When Mr. Chen was tired of painting, he would often go to the Wu Yuan teahouse in Guanqian to relax. But the teahouse had many regular customers, and regular customers often asked for paintings. Paintings piled up for months or even years. When they saw Mr. Chen coming, they would surround him and urge him to pay his debt. Painting debt was worse than money debt. Mr. Chen could not cope and did not dare to go to the Wu Yuan teahouse for more than ten days. He often visited ancient sites in the suburbs, picking up old things at cold stalls, as a refuge for absconding. Children running away from school is what they have been used to hear. Mr. Chen flees from painting, is truly a strange tale in the art world, and can be laughed at. Mr. Chen was humorous and corpulent, resembling a Luohan. He was a model in the Leng Hong Society. Many people followed him to study painting. The novelist Cheng Xiaoqing and the younger brother of Yanqiao, Ji Qian, were all his disciples. I studied at Caoqiao School and was once bathed in his spring breeze.

Warmth in the Heart (379)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Seventeen: Having the Skills to Maintain Youth, Cui Dai Blends Eyebrows; Having No Way to Prolong Life, the Golden Market Races for Valiant Bones

That director was also from the South and was very sincere, but he was specifically inviting guests for Hua Lao Liu. He was an economist. He had calculated a little and thought that this gambling game was specially set up for Hua Lao Liu. The money drawn from the top could be said to be to support Hua Lao Liu. Even if the top money was not enough, if he won a little himself, he could make up a total of two or three thousand yuan, which would be a respectable amount. Who knew that things in the world often exceeded expectations? As a result, the host lost heavily. Not only did he lose everything, but he also lost all the top money. After everyone dispersed, the host felt very disappointed. Originally, Hua Lao Liu also knew that this gambling game was specially set up for him, and he felt very sorry. Not only did he not get any money himself, but he also dragged the host down, causing him to lose a large sum. He said that it was all his, Hua Lao Liu's, bad luck. Not only was he unlucky, but he also dragged others down. However, the host comforted him, saying that we gamblers win and lose all the time, it's not a big deal. You don't have to mind. He also signed a check for five hundred yuan for Hua Lao Liu, saying that he had kept him up all night and returned empty-handed, which would inevitably bring bad luck. In the next few days, my luck is not good. When my luck is better, I will think of a way for you. However, gamblers value superstition the most. Many people who are usually very open-minded have many superstitions when it comes to gambling. That director lost money, but he didn't blame himself. Instead, he blamed Hua Lao Liu. He thought that he had also supported the girls from the South before, someone so and so, and was very satisfied. He even won money himself. How could he lose so much today? Maybe she is a slow-witted person. No wonder her business is not good. She is probably going through a black period. Gamblers pay very close attention to red and black. Therefore, whenever there is gambling, they no longer call for Hua Yuan Chun's card. In addition, after spreading the word among many gambling friends, Hua Lao Liu could not find wealthy gamblers. Since he could not find wealthy gamblers, his city card gradually decreased. A month later, although Ye Tonghou came, he is now a businessman. The friends he knows are not first-class characters. But he couldn't ignore Hua Lao Liu's kindness, so he went to have a drink once and played a few games of cards. It was just ordinary socializing. Moreover, his branch is in Tianjin, and he often has to go to Tianjin. In a blink of an eye, Hua Yuan Chun had been in Beijing for more than half a year. However, his business did not improve much. When he had a little money, he couldn't save it. His original intention was to return to Shanghai when he had saved some money. But he could not fulfill his wish. The two good friends in Shanghai often wrote letters, plucking at his heartstrings, and he could not help but think of the red beans of Jiangnan. In this depressed mood, he suddenly fell ill.

Oil Market: Asphalt Takes Off Suddenly

▲Rising by More Than Four Taels in Half a Month

Before the closing of accounts, the situation for asphalt was peaceful. However, after the closing of accounts, it suddenly took off, with the market taking off suddenly. In just half a month, it rose by more than four taels, a rare spectacle since the market opened. The reason is that the various production areas in Northwest Hubei suffered a definite 20% reduction in harvest last year, which has not been seen in nearly 20 years. As a result, when the spring sales were about to begin, there were no goods to supply. The market situation changed abruptly. According to the details in yesterday's letter from Hankou, heavily judged products have already sold for 19 taels and 3-4 qian, and Qianping Macheng oil also requires 19 taels. The source is extremely scarce. Those who are looking to procure goods are coming one after another. The later situation will not improve. The spring market has changed to such an extent, which was completely unimaginable. It is not possible to predict what process will be taken in the future to increase to what extent. It can be said to be a new era not seen in the open market. The price of Zhilu Pingnei oil has also reached beyond 30 yuan per stone at the Hangzhou exchange. The Jiaxing people in this province are even more unique, and selling in Shanghai must not be less than 31 yuan. Moreover, the existing stock in the entire production area is only slightly over 3,000, so scarcity makes it even more expensive. The existing Shanghai firms were not very thick when the accounts were settled. They were hoping to purchase a batch from Hankou after the settlement. Unexpectedly, the Hankou market had no stock, so it was unable to supply the buying households, resulting in a collective regret. The Shanghai firms were even more disappointed. It is said that several of them still have large short positions that have not been covered, so the losses are even more unbearable. Therefore, it can be said that the Shanghai market has no inventory at all, and the selling price has already been increased. Each firm only has goods to sell.

Yesterday, All Sectors Held a Memorial Service for Fallen Soldiers

▲Over 30,000 Attendees at the Venue

▲City-wide Entertainment Shut Down for One Day

For the sake of national unification and the beginning of political tutelage, the National Government, commemorating the revolutionary martyrs who sacrificed for the party and the country, specifically designated yesterday for the entire country to unanimously commemorate the fallen soldiers, in order to comfort their spirits in the underworld and to celebrate their meritorious deeds after death. After receiving the central government's telegram, the Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special City Party Department immediately sent personnel to actively prepare in conjunction with the Garrison Command, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and others. At 8:00 a.m. yesterday, it convened people from all walks of life at the West Gate Public Sports Field to hold the city's memorial service for fallen soldiers. At the same time, it notified all citizens of the city to wear black gauze armbands for one day and to stop banquets and entertainment for one day. Starting yesterday, all organs, groups, and schools raised their flags at half-mast for three days. At 8:00 a.m., the Navy fired 33 artillery rounds, and all factories in the city sounded their whistles three times to express mourning. In addition, various organs, party departments at all levels, groups, and schools held separate memorial services. The details are recorded as follows:

Memorial Service for Fallen Soldiers Photography

(Photographed by this newspaper)

Convention Circumstances: Commemorative Meeting Venue Established at

the Public Sports Field. The decorations were extremely somber and solemn. ▲ Eulogies from Various Sectors: On this, the tenth day of March in the twentieth year of the Republic of China, the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters of the Chinese Kuomintang, the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Songhu Garrison Command, and all circles of Shanghai, with the deepest sorrow, offer this eulogy before the spirits of the fallen soldiers of the National Revolutionary Army who died in the suppression of the rebellion, saying: Alas, the wind is mournful, the sun scorching, the sky gloomy, and the ghosts weeping. Since ancient times, it has been thus; what remedy is there? In the past, warmongers treated war as a game. There were only sacrifices, but no guiding principles. Only our righteous army, with aspirations for revolution, united in hatred against the enemy, rose up with thunderous speed. Emerging from Lingnan and the coast, they struck directly at Yanyou, unifying the land before a year had passed. Punishing the guilty and comforting the people, tracing back to Tang and Wu, once they donned their armor, blood flowed so profusely it could float pestles. Heaven and earth are not benevolent; metal and stone evolve. Killing people like cutting hemp, no longer with mere sticks and blades, but with smoke, bullets, and rain, flesh and blood flying in all directions. Disregarding their own safety, they crushed the stubborn enemy. With one heart and mind, unwavering in the face of danger, valuing purpose over life, honoring name over existence. Cold rises from the Yi River, and the brave soldiers do not return. Great indeed are the national martyrs, heavier than Mount Tai. The whales and giant sea creatures have been sealed away, and the apes and cranes have transformed. Sprinkle your azure blood to support this Chinese land. Bows and swords move on their own, killing brigands as if hearing their commands. Even in death, they can still fight. Such is their spirit. The old capital has been recovered, and great disasters have been quelled. A joyous drink from the Yellow Dragon Cup, may it comfort your loyal souls. Alas, so many heroes, the elite of the Party and the nation. The whole world mourns; though dead, you live on. Slowly waving flags and banners, lingering drums of war, recalling your valor and sacrifice, tears fall like rain. From all directions, we gather, offering clean hearts and fragrant incense. May your departed spirits not be far away, but come to partake and enjoy this offering. ▲ Mayor Zhang's Speech: What day is today? It is the day to commemorate the fallen soldiers who died suppressing the rebellion. Recalling that since the National Revolutionary Army advanced to the Yangtze River and established its capital in Nanjing, it has been five or six years, during which countless hardships and numerous fierce battles were endured before achieving today's success in unification. Now, the whole country is united, and the foundation of the nation is gradually secure. The future is bright and just beginning to flourish. But tracing back to how we achieved this newly emerging situation, we cannot but say that it is the result of the struggle of the revolutionary heroes on the battlefield. During the period of military administration, the emphasis was on fighting against evil forces, and the figures who fought against these forces relied on all the revolutionary heroes on the battlefield. Therefore, since the suppression of the rebellion, the soldiers at the front lines, upholding the spirit of the Three Principles of the People and following the teachings of the late Premier, advanced one after another, striving bravely to be the first, sacrificing countless heads and shedding countless amounts of blood to construct this newly emerging nation. Then, we, who live in peace and think of danger, reflecting on the past and remembering the present, how can we not feel sorrow and longing for the spirit of the soldiers who sacrificed themselves in suppressing the rebellion over the years? The prosperity of a nation or the unification of a country cannot be achieved by a single throw of a hand or a single step of a foot, and even less can it be achieved in a year or six months, or by the strength of one or two people. If we want the prosperity of the nation and the unification of the country, there must be a cost involved. What is the so-called cost? It is sacrifice. Sacrifice is a necessary condition before a cause can succeed. This is true of all undertakings, and especially true of revolutionary undertakings. If we want to eliminate evil forces, there must be what is called struggle, and in the process of struggle, there cannot but be the cost of sacrifice. Similarly, if we want to build a new country, we must consume countless amounts of spiritual and material resources, and this kind of consumption can also be called sacrifice. Therefore, in the first half of the revolution, there must be the sacrifice of fighting against evil forces, and in the second half of the revolution, there must be spiritual and material sacrifices in building a new country. Today, tracing the special merits of the fallen soldiers who suppressed the rebellion, they were indeed the ones who undertook the complete work of the first half of the revolutionary history. If we do not fight against evil forces, then evil forces cannot be eliminated, and the opportunity to build a new country will never come. Therefore, all the new emerging opportunities of today are bestowed by the sacrifices of the fallen soldiers who suppressed the rebellion. Living in the present and thinking about the situation of the soldiers sacrificing themselves on the battlefield at that time, as the ancients said, each one was worth ten, their shouts shook the heavens, their livers and brains smeared the central plains, their blood and marrow covered the wild grass, risking death without hesitation, all these are true portraits of the fallen soldiers. Alas, forgetting the past is betraying the future. Since the work of sacrifice and struggle of the soldiers was so great and difficult, how can we not rise up and pursue it, striving to devote our heart and strength to the Party and the nation to comfort the spirits of the soldiers in the netherworld? Moreover, even more importantly, if we want to commemorate or remember the fallen soldiers, we should not only conduct formal commemorations and remembrances, but also continue their spirit of sacrifice. As mentioned earlier, the fallen soldiers undertook the work of the first half of the revolutionary history, but the work of the second half of the revolutionary history, the so-called work of building a new country, has not yet been completed. Therefore, we know that our responsibility today is to unite and work together to undertake the great responsibility of building a new country, following the path shown by the Three Principles of the People, following all the teachings of the late Premier, regardless of the degree of spiritual and material sacrifice, gradually step by step, to complete the ultimate goal of building a new country. If we are truly like this, then we will be able to commemorate the spirit of sacrifice of the fallen soldiers who suppressed the rebellion forever, and the new country under the Three Principles of the People will perhaps have a day of complete realization soon.

He Jiwu's Account of the Wuchang Incident

▲ Steps in the Development of China National Aviation Corporation

Yesterday, a telegram from Jiujiang reported that the China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) aircraft "Wuchang" crashed in Xunyang, but the passengers were unharmed. A journalist from the Guowen News Agency visited He Jiwu, the General Manager of CNAC, to inquire about the details and the company's recent situation. He Jiwu informed him of the following details and the company's recent status.

▲ The Wuchang Aircraft had sustained minor damage in Hankou, so the three passengers had already refunded their tickets in Hankou and were not on board. The aircraft was only being flown empty to Shanghai for repairs. At 1:00 PM on the afternoon of the 8th, while passing through Jiujiang, it was hit by wind and the fuselage fell. It immediately stopped in Jiangxi. Fortunately, the navy warship Weisheng sent a艇 to rescue it. The aircraft was transported to Shanghai by the Taikoo Company's Whangpoo轮 and has now been sent to the Longhua Aircraft Factory for repairs. The pilot, Zhou Huang, also arrived in Shanghai at the same time.

▲ Inspecting various air stations: Mr. He himself had taken a flight from Shanghai on the 6th of this month (last Friday) to inspect the airfields in Nanjing, Wuhu, Anqing, Jiujiang, and Hankou, and urged improvements in the equipment at each station. On the 9th, he returned to Shanghai on the Jiujiang aircraft.

▲ Company's plans: The company's current plan is to first extend the Shanghai-Chengdu line to Yichang, then start the Beijing-Ping (Beiping) air route, then extend the Shanghai-Chengdu line to Chongqing, then start the Shanghai-Guangdong air route, and finally complete the Shanghai-Chengdu air route directly to Chengdu. These are the steps in the plan.

▲ Developing the Shanghai-Chengdu line: As for the detailed arrangements for each route, the Shanghai-Chengdu line can fly from Hankou to Yichang on the 16th of this month. A pontoon (i.e., a停机标志) is being installed on the river surface in Shashi between Hankou and Yichang. It should be completed by the 23rd of this month, and then it will be able to land at each station. Within three months, it will be able to fly to Chongqing. Because the air pressure in Sichuan is slightly different from that in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, the company's existing single-engine aircraft cannot fly safely. It has now ordered two twin-engine aircraft from the United States, worth approximately 45,000 US dollars. The transportation from Chengdu to Chongqing is more convenient than from Chongqing to Hankou, so it is okay to fly there slightly later.

▲ Beijing-Ping mail: The Beijing-Ping line was originally planned to start flying on the 15th of this month, but because the Jinan air station has not yet been completed and the radio has not yet been installed, the date has been postponed to April 1st for the official opening. The Xuzhou radio will be able to communicate with Shanghai within a few days. Nie Kaiyi flew a trial flight to Beiping and is now in Tianjin. He can return to Shanghai within a week. The company's original contract with the post office was for domestic mail to be transported by the company. Now the Ministry of Communications has revised the contract so that the Beijing-Ping line remains the same, but the route from Shanghai directly to the Northeast is now transported by Eurasia Aviation Corporation.

籌辦滬粤綫: The Shanghai-Guangdong line can be completed in about six months, passing through Ningbo, Wenzhou, Xiamen, Shantou, and then Guangzhou. It is planned to take two days to fly there. Twin-engine aircraft have also been ordered. Initially, four aircraft will be needed to fly back and forth. The installation of radio equipment along the stations is currently being planned. The order for these aircraft will be placed after the twin-engine aircraft flying from Shanghai to Chongqing have arrived.

Silk Factory Industry Submits Petition to Change Silk Industry Bond Amount

▲ Representative Chu Fucheng Goes to Beijing for Second Petition

The silk factory industry in the three regions of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai sent Chu Fucheng, their second petition representative, to Beijing yesterday with a written petition regarding the silk industry bond issue. He took the 2:50 PM special express train. Representative Wang Xiaolai, due to personal matters, departed this morning (the 11th) on an early express train. The original text of the petition to the National Government is reproduced below.

Regarding the petition for approval to issue silk industry bonds, failing to provide relief, resulting in an excessive burden, requesting the maintenance of the original bond amount, and amending the regulations. We, the silk factory industry of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai, due to the decline of the silk market, are on the verge of bankruptcy. We have appealed for the issuance of silk industry bonds for relief and have received approval to issue bonds worth 8 million yuan, with 6 million yuan for short-term relief to silk merchants and 2 million yuan for long-term fundamental improvement of sericulture. Subsequently, we read in the newspaper that the Legislative Yuan has amended the regulations for the 1931 Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Bond, setting the amount at 6 million yuan, with one-third for rewarding raw silk exports, one-third for improving silk factory machinery, and one-third for improving sericulture. From the date of issuance, the Jianghai Customs will collect a special tax of 22.5 yuan per dan on raw silk exports as a fund for repaying the principal and interest, to be repaid in seven years and six months. The manufacturers believe that the relief obtained is minimal and the responsibilities are excessive, which will not alleviate the current emergency but will leave future worries. Therefore, representatives were publicly elected to go to Beijing to state the facts and request changes, hoping to gain insight from your esteemed court (ministry). We believe that the silk factory industry in the three regions of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai suffered overall losses last year and found it difficult to maintain operations. Apart from a few who obtained accommodation from the silver and money industry, accepting mortgaged dry cocoons and borrowing to start operations, most have stopped operations to await relief. In January of this year, the price once increased sharply, reaching 1,080 taels per dan, but within a few days, it fell back to less than 1,000 taels. However, the cost of raw materials is 950 taels, various labor costs are 250 taels, and interest, profit sharing, insurance, and warehouse rent are 100 taels, totaling at least 1,300 taels. Therefore, each dan of silk must lose more than 300 taels. Without adequate relief, not only will most silk factories be forced to close, but the loss of this sales channel during the new cocoon season will have a significant impact on farmers' livelihoods and social finance. Therefore, even if the relief measures cannot be fully adequate, they must allow room for turnover. This is the first reason for requesting a change in the bond amount. As for improving machinery, it is indeed an important goal. However, the Italian reeling machines commonly used for Chinese silk are not fundamentally unsuitable. Foreign sales are mainly to the United States and France, and France still enjoys using silk reeled by Italian machines. The reason why it cannot compete with Japanese silk is that management rights cannot be effectively implemented and workers do not accept guidance. Reeling machines for silk were originally created in Italy, and because their products are used by European and American buyers, there has been no change to this day. Based on this, the improvement of machinery is not urgent. Furthermore, most silk factories rent their factories, and the machinery is owned by the landlord as equipment with the house. Even if we want to reform them, our government can order the landlords to gradually renovate them. However, there are facts that cannot be ignored. Once the machinery is changed, its manufacturing methods will naturally be different. It is not possible to train tens of thousands of female workers to master the technology overnight. This is the second reason for requesting a change in the bond amount. After repeated consultations, we can only rely on your esteemed court (ministry) to understand the critical situation of the silk factory industry, approve the change in allocation, maintain the original bond amount of 8 million yuan, with 6 million yuan for relief to silk merchants and 2 million yuan for improving sericulture, and consult the Legislative Yuan to amend the regulations for promulgation and release the silk merchants from their urgent plight. In addition to this petition, we hereby submit this petition, requesting your examination and implementation, and await your order with utmost urgency. Committee of the Shanghai Silk Factory Industry Association, Committee of the Wuxi County Silk Factory Industry Association, Preparatory Committee of the Zhejiang Silk Factory Federation, respectfully presented.

Zhabei Public Bus Patronizes Cake Shops and Iron Shops

▲ Similar to public buses in the foreign concessions

▲ Cake stall ovens and iron shop apprentices suffer

Last Saturday and Sunday, a public bus of Route 9 of the Public Concession crashed into the reception room at No. 602, the corner of Avenue Foch and Avenue du Roi Albert, which was a topic of conversation for a while. Unexpectedly, three days later, a similar incident occurred in Zhabei. However, the places patronized by the bus were not reception rooms but cake stalls and iron shops. It can be said that there are coincidences in car accidents. This incident occurred at around 3 p.m. yesterday. A Huashang public bus, Route 3, No. 4011, traveling in Zhabei, was driving west along No. 1466, Qujiang Road, when, for some unknown reason, the machinery suddenly became uncontrollable. The front of the bus swerved to the left, causing it to knock over the oven of the cake stall set up by Zhang Xingbang at No. 1466. The pillars in front of the door were also shaken and broken. However, the engine failed to brake, and it continued to move forward, causing the Xiao Shuntai iron shop at No. 1468 to also suffer. Wang Xuerong, an apprentice standing at the door doing work, was run over by the wheel and fell to the ground in pain. Passengers in the bus were shocked by the sight and got out of the bus one after another. The front of the bus was also damaged due to excessive shock, and the machinery broke down, making it impossible to drive any further. Police officers from the Zhongxing Road police station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau immediately went to investigate everything after hearing the news. Wang Xuerong, the iron shop apprentice who was run over, was sent to the hospital for treatment by the shop owner, but his injuries were severe and he was in critical condition.

Youth Disgusted with the World Attempts Suicide in the Huangpu River

▲ Recently wrote a municipal book

▲ Doesn't know if the bookstore will accept it

▲ Future is bleak, hence the suicide attempt

At 6 p.m. the day before yesterday, a young man hired a No. 609 sampan at the Yangjingbang wharf, claiming to cross over to the British warship anchored in the center of the Huangpu River. The boatman asked for four dimes as a round-trip fare, and the young man paid the full amount. Unexpectedly, after leaving the shore for five or six zhang, he suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. Fortunately, he was rescued on the spot by the boatman and sent to the water police station. After questioning, he stated that his name was Shen Daoyuan, 22 years old, from Wuxi, and that his home was at No. 34, Yingya Pavilion, in the city of his hometown. His father's name was Jinhua, and he ran a Demaosen silk and cloth shop outside the North Gate of his hometown. There was one elder brother and one younger brother in the family. The elder brother worked in the shop, and the younger brother was still studying. He himself had studied at a certain university in Wusong but had not yet graduated. He dropped out of school due to some reasons, stayed at home, and felt extremely bored. In his spare time, he did some writing and submitted it to various magazines or newspapers for publication. He recently wrote a municipal book, about a hundred pages long. This morning (i.e., the morning before yesterday), he took five yuan from home as travel expenses, carried the book, and bid farewell to his mother to come to Shanghai by car, intending to submit it to a bookstore for publication. He spent one and a half yuan on the car fare. After arriving in Shanghai, he stayed in a three-yuan room at the Shenzhou Hotel on the Fourth Avenue, with only half a yuan left for spending. In the afternoon, he took the book to a certain bookstore on the Fourth Avenue to discuss the matter. After the bookstore took the book, they said that they would reply within three days whether or not to accept it. When he left the bookstore, he suddenly felt dizzy and thought that he had no permanent job at present and that the future was difficult to predict. It would be better to leave this evil world as soon as possible, so he jumped into the river to seek death. According to his statement, the head of the police ordered him to stay in the police station for the night. Yesterday morning, he ordered Detective Huang Songsheng to send him to the Wuxi Fellow-Villagers Association to find a way to send him back to his hometown.

Ministry of Communications Approves Increase in Dredging Surtax for Dredging the Shoal

▲ Charge three percent of the value according to the new tax rate

▲ Collection to begin on April 1st

The Ministry of Communications recently saw reports that the Dredging Bureau planned to increase the dredging surtax on import taxes for dredging the Shoal, and had inquired with the Ministry of Finance whether it had been filed. It is now heard that the Dredging Bureau recently received a letter from Mr. Meierle, the Chief Inspector of Customs, stating that the dredging surtax collected by the Dredging Bureau in the import tax for dredging the Shoal had been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval. Now, the Ministry of Finance has issued an order stating that the dredging tax collected by the Dredging Bureau has always been 3% of the value according to the old tax rules. Now, regarding the proposal to increase the surtax for dredging the Shoal, it is approved to charge 3% of the value according to the current new tax rate. It is expected to be followed accordingly. It is heard that the Chief Inspector of Customs has ordered the Jianghai Customs to start collecting it on April 1st.

Embezzlement of Customs Treasury Bonds and Drafts

▲ Huang Yinting Sentenced to Eight Months Imprisonment

Huang Yinting, a Cantonese who had been an employee of the National Bank for three years, changed his career to a public debt broker after resigning. In November last year, Zheng Jiaju, a clerk at the National Bank, and Luo Peiren, an employee of the Shanghai Trust Company, entrusted him with the sale of 50 Customs Treasury Bonds and drafts worth more than 5,000 yuan in the 19th year of the Republic. Huang embezzled them. Zheng and others asked for them without success and reported to the General Police Station, ordering detectives to arrest Huang and send him to the Special District Local Court for interrogation and detention. The day before yesterday morning, Judge Xu Jiaxi opened a court session to continue the trial. The plaintiff Zheng Jiaju complained about the previous situation and attached a private prosecution, requesting compensation of 10,000 yuan in Customs Treasury Bonds from the 19th year of the Republic. When questioned, the defendant confessed that he had suffered losses in the operation of public debt and that the drafts had been deducted by the trading house, so he could not return them. He also hired a lawyer to defend him. Judge Xu obtained the confession and sentenced the defendant to eight months' imprisonment for embezzling objects in his business possession and ordered him to compensate the plaintiff for 10,000 yuan in Customs Treasury Bonds from the 19th year of the Republic.

Shanghai Bank Adds Chinese Traveler's Checks

The Shanghai Bank previously had a type of traveler's check in four denominations: ten yuan, twenty yuan, fifty yuan, and one hundred yuan. The traveler's signature was required as proof, and when cashing, the signature had to be verified to match before it could be cashed, as a guarantee for the traveler's expenses. Even if it was lost en route, it would not be obtained. People from all walks of life thought it was very convenient. However, the previously issued checks were all in Western languages, and those who were not familiar with Western languages had regrets. It is now heard that in order to benefit travelers and provide universal service, the bank has specially added Chinese traveler's checks, also in four denominations: ten yuan, twenty yuan, fifty yuan, and one hundred yuan. Type A is one hundred yuan, the check pattern is red. Type B is fifty yuan, the pattern is purple. Type C is twenty yuan, the pattern is green. Type D is ten yuan, the pattern is light green. They have been issued since February 15th. During this spring outing season, users are very convenient.

Shunheng Foreign Company Loses Two Ships in Accidents

▲ Huge losses

▲ Talico Ship Blown Up and Sunk

A month ago, the Shunheng Foreign Company had a cargo ship named S.S. Trecolor, which set off from Hamburg, Germany, directly to Shanghai. The ship was fully loaded with dangerous explosives. It was loaded to Shanghai for unloading. When the ship arrived outside the port of Colombo in Ceylon, the white medicine loaded in the middle compartment suddenly exploded due to the heat, the middle compartment was breached, and the ship sank into the sea. Many crew members and sailors were injured in the explosion. Unexpectedly, on the third day after sinking into the sea, the gunpowder and bullets in the front and rear compartments exploded a second time on the seabed, causing the ship to be completely destroyed. The ammunition and weapons that were intended to be salvaged were completely lost. The value of the goods reached ten million yuan, and the loss of the ship was also over one million. The matter has been notified to the main recipient of the goods purchased by our country who handled the goods.

▲ Roseville Ship Runs Aground

The Roseville of the Shunheng Foreign Company was carrying a large batch of American timber and salted fish from the Pacific Ocean to Shanghai. After arriving in Shanghai, 70% of the Shanghai cargo was unloaded, and the remaining 30% was transferred to Xiamen and Hong Kong for unloading. The ship left Shanghai for Hong Kong on the morning of the 7th. When it reached the sea off Fuzhou, about 60 nautical miles from the island of Dnabu (transliteration) in Hong Kong, it suddenly encountered a thick fog. The navigation route was obscured by the fog. The captain, Johnson, mistakenly steered the ship onto a reef outside the island. The bottom of the ship ran into the reef and was immediately breached. Seawater then entered. The captain, fearing that the ship would sink immediately, steered the ship onto the reef so that it could be grounded and not sink. He urgently sent a radio message to Shanghai for help. After receiving the news, the Shanghai Bureau transferred the message to the Hong Kong line because Hong Kong was closer, and asked them to send a tugboat to rescue the ship as soon as possible.

▲ All Crew Members Rescued

Yesterday, the line continued to receive a telegram from the ship stating that the ship had gradually sunk into the sea, and the seawater had reached the deck. The cargo in the compartments had been submerged in the water. The barge sent by the port had not been able to unload the cargo. The crew members and sailors, a total of 37 people, were fortunate to be in the daytime when the accident occurred. They each took lifeboats and scrambled to escape to the sea. Fortunately, there was a lighthouse nearby, and the crew members had gathered to the mountain on the lighthouse to wait for the rescue ship. All of them survived and none were killed. Yesterday, the captain, Johnson, also left the ship. Everyone barely escaped. After the Hong Kong barge arrived, it took the captain and crew members on the mountain back to Hong Kong. The ship was too badly damaged to be towed and rescued. Yesterday, an employee of the line told a reporter that the situation of this ship was equal to Xinchang, and it would probably sink completely into the sea after some time. The ship's carrying capacity was 8,000 tons, and the public and private losses, including cargo and crew luggage, were at least one million yuan. Both ships were insured, and Shunheng had no losses.

Special Maritime News

▲ Japanese Ship Encounters Danger

The Honghai Maru, a cargo ship of the Japanese Osaka Marine Fire Insurance Company, has a carrying capacity of 1,300 tons. This time, it set off from Tianjin to Shanghai and could arrive in four days as usual. However, after crossing the river, the ship encountered strong winds and fog at sea, making navigation difficult. It was unprecedented. It was in a dangerous situation several times in the frightening wind and waves. Fortunately, the captain and crew members worked hard to support it and were able to avoid sinking. Yesterday, the ship arrived in Shanghai, and the captain and crew members were grateful for their survival. The captain went to the Japanese consulate to report the situation of the disaster and planned to unload the coal and inspect the bottom of the ship for damage.

▲ More News About Xinchang

It is now heard that the Xinchang ship has sunk into the sea, with only one smokestack exposed above the water. Regarding the loss of crew members' luggage, the bureau will issue subsidies according to the example of the Xinjin disaster. As for salvaging the ship, it will be decided after the divers who were sent to inspect the seabed at the place of the accident return to Shanghai to report. The ship's machinery is excellent and it has been decided to dismantle it and transport it to Shanghai. If it is impossible to salvage it, the method of dismantling it by sections will be carried out.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Prepares for National Assembly Representative Elections

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce is commencing preparations for the election of Shanghai representatives to the National Assembly. The details are recorded below:

▲Collecting Registration Books: The Chamber of Commerce has dispatched clerk Zhou Songxun from the Document Section to the Election Office to collect the various registration books for the election. A total of four types of books were collected: (1) Organization Report Book, (2) Articles of Association Page, (3) Brief Biography Form of Officials, (4) Member List. In addition to these four types of books, several blank pages were also included.

▲Separately Expediting Preparation: After receiving the various registration books, the Chamber of Commerce noted that the Election Office had set a deadline of the 15th of this month for submission. Therefore, the Secretariat is separately completing and submitting them. The Articles of Association and Organization Report are being handled by the Document Section of the General Affairs Department, while the Brief Biography Form of Officials and the Member List are being handled by the Registration Section of the Business Department.

Notice to Members: The Chamber of Commerce yesterday issued a notice to all industry guilds and shop employee members in the city, stating that according to the attached schedule of the National Assembly Representative Election Implementation Law promulgated by the National Government, Shanghai representatives should be elected by the Chamber of Commerce and industrial organizations. The various election registration books have already been collected by the Chamber and sent to the Shanghai Election Office for National Assembly Representatives. The number of representatives for each industry guild and shop member who is a member of the association should be completed and submitted according to the prescribed format. However, the qualification for representative election is limited to those guilds and shops that have been legally registered. All members are hereby notified that those who have not yet registered with the Social Affairs Bureau should promptly complete the registration procedures in accordance with the following order before the 15th of this month: (1) Fill in the total capital amount, pay the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce membership fee for the 19th year, and obtain the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce membership certificate. (2) Present the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce membership certificate, along with the association's articles of association and a list of members and officials, to the Social Affairs Bureau for registration and issuance of a license. If there are any unclear points regarding the above procedures, please feel free to inquire with the Business Department of the Chamber of Commerce at any time. This matter concerns the election policy, so please do not delay or be negligent. This is of utmost importance. This notice is hereby given.

Shanghai Municipal Council Sets Date for Foreign Board Elections

The Dalu News reports that the polling place for this year's election of foreign directors and land commissioners of the Shanghai Municipal Council has been decided to be at the Shanghai Municipal Council's Rates Office. The voting time is set for the 16th and 17th, both from 10:00 AM to 3:00 PM.

Japanese Commercial Official Announces Sino-Japanese Trade Figures for February

According to the Sino-Japanese trade figures for February announced by the Japanese Commercial Counselor's Office in Shanghai, Japanese goods exported to China were valued at 18 million Japanese yen, while Chinese goods exported to Japan were valued at 16 million Japanese yen. From China's perspective, this represents a trade deficit of 2 million yen. If combined with the figures for January, the total trade deficit is 4 million yen. However, this is a significant decrease of 12 million yen compared to the same period in the second year. Furthermore, Japan's total foreign trade shows imports valued at 97 million yen and exports valued at 91 million yen, resulting in a trade deficit of 6 million yen. Offsetting this against the trade surplus in January, the total trade deficit for the two months is 5 million yen, representing a remarkable decrease of 73 million yen compared to the same period in the previous year, which is an unusual phenomenon.

Second Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Women's National Goods Association

▲Decision on Procedures for School Students to Join

After the first joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Shanghai Women's National Goods Promotion Association, the appointed directors of each group have been working diligently on association affairs. The second joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees was held yesterday at 4:00 PM. Attendees included Zheng Huichen, Tang Guanyu, Lin Kecong, Shu Huizhen, Liang Jiuguang, Chen Hongbi, Ouyang Jun, Chen Hongru, Zhou Jun, Ma Yuying (representing Tang Guanyu), Chen Jingrong, Ge Jinghe (representing Chen Jingrong), Han Jingnong, Ding Lude, Tang Nai, and over ten others. Chairman Zhou Jun reported on the work of each group and announced the detailed rules for each group of the Executive Committee, which were unanimously approved. Chen Jingrong reported on the accounting records. Lin Kecong of the Propaganda Group reported on the process of soliciting students from various schools to join, with over ten schools, including Peiwen, Zhirenyong, Nanyang Girls' High School, Aiguo, and Southeast Physical Education College, expressing their willingness to join and take on propaganda duties. The meeting then discussed the procedures for students to join the association: (1) They must be 15 years of age or older. (2) The membership fee is waived, and the annual fee is 20 cents per person. Each school is considered a group, and each group may send a representative to attend meetings. Those who voluntarily join individually will still follow the regular procedures. However, teachers in the schools must be counted as members.

Candidates for Shanghai Municipal Council Foreign Board Express Political Views

The Zi Lin News reports that Okamoto of Japan and Peier and Xiebade of England, three candidates for the Shanghai Municipal Council board, have expressed their opinions. Okamoto does not support the Shanghai Municipal Council's acquisition of the Dagua Hotel property or the sale of the existing council site because it is located in a remote western area with high land prices, and there is no need to relocate the Shanghai Municipal Council site. Regarding the lack of open space in the western district, he believes that other districts in the concession are more densely populated and therefore have a greater need for open spaces. As for the issue of roads extending beyond the boundaries, he believes that the assistance of the consular corps is necessary to achieve a solution. He strongly advocates for transparency in municipal affairs and proposes that the Shanghai Municipal Council should establish a public information department, similar to those in major Western cities. He believes that the current practice of only reporting major events to the public is outdated. Peier will delay expressing his opinion on the Dagua Hotel issue but strongly opposes the sale of the existing Shanghai Municipal Council site. He also advocates for the urgent addition of open spaces in the northern and eastern districts and strongly supports transparency in municipal affairs, agreeing with the establishment of a public information department. Xiebade has not expressed any opinion on the issues of acquiring the Dagua Hotel and selling the Shanghai Municipal Council site. Regarding transparency in municipal affairs, he believes that the current practices have no shortcomings and does not support the establishment of a public information department. He has accepted the proposal to add open spaces in the northern and eastern districts in principle but believes that the only thing lacking is funding. Regarding the issue of building roads beyond the boundaries, he believes that the Chinese authorities should allow the situation to remain as it is before a practical solution is agreed upon.

Provisional Executive Committee of the National Physicians' Association

The National Physicians' Association convened a provisional executive committee meeting at its office yesterday, chaired by Xu Nili, to discuss the following: (1) A letter from the Hangzhou Physicians and Pharmacists Association stated that the new medicine business tax rate in Zhejiang Province is excessively high and exceeds normal standards, requesting the Association to petition the Ministry of Finance to order the Provincial Department of Finance to revise it accordingly. It was resolved to do so and the matter was handed over to the Document Committee to draft a document. (2) The Wuhan Physicians' Association stated that hospitals and clinics are also subject to the local business tax regulations, requesting the Association to unanimously advocate for exemption. It was resolved that the imposition of business tax on hospitals and clinics in that area is not stipulated in the original regulations. Moreover, hospitals and clinics are of a charitable nature and use technology to earn profits, which is different from other businesses. After verifying the original regulations, a response will be sent to the Wuhan Physicians' Association, and unanimous advocacy for exemption will be made. (3) The Ningyan Physicians' Association requested the Association to research and discuss whether the Japanese medicine "Manimarin" is harmful to those who use it to quit smoking. It was resolved that if the medicine is used as indicated in the instructions, it should not harm the body of those who quit smoking. Side effects may occur due to individual circumstances. The association will respond to the Ningyan Physicians’ Association with this information. (4) Committee member Wang Qizhang submitted an opinion on the Western medicine physician examination regulations announced by the Examination Yuan, requesting discussion by various medical associations. It was resolved to forward it to the Shanghai Physicians' Association to be published in the "New Medicine and Society" column of the Shishi Xinbao (Eastern Times) for public discussion by various medical associations. The meeting adjourned at 6:00 PM.
